     <p>
      <b>
       Nepal
      </b>
      (
      <span class="nowrap">
       <span class="noexcerpt">
        <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a4/En-us-Nepal.ogg" title="Listen">
         <img alt="Listen" data-file-height="11" data-file-width="11" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
        </a>
        <sup>
         <span class="IPA" style="color:#00e;font:bold 80% sans-serif;padding:0 .1em">
          <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Nepal.ogg" title="File:En-us-Nepal.ogg">
           i
          </a>
         </span>
        </sup>
       </span>
       <span class="IPA nopopups">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">
         /
         <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
          <span title="'n' in 'no'">
           n
          </span>
          <span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">
           ə
          </span>
          <span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">
           ˈ
          </span>
          <span title="'p' in 'pie'">
           p
          </span>
          <span title="/ɔː/ 'au' in 'fraud'">
           ɔː
          </span>
          <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
           l
          </span>
         </span>
         /
        </a>
       </span>
      </span>
      ;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        [9]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">
       Nepali
      </a>
      :
      <span lang="ne">
       नेपाल
      </span>
      <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Nepali transliteration">
       <span class="unicode haudio">
        <span class="fn">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nepal.ogg" title="About this sound">
           <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9b/Nepal.ogg" title="Nepal.ogg">
          <i>
           Nepāl
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
      </span>
      <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
       <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
        [neˈpal]
       </a>
      </span>
      ), officially the
      <b>
       Federal Democratic Republic of Nepal
      </b>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">
       Nepali
      </a>
      :
      <span lang="ne">
       सङ्घीय लोकतान्त्रिक गणतन्त्र नेपाल
      </span>
      <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Nepali transliteration">
       <i>
        Sanghiya Loktāntrik Ganatantra Nepāl
       </i>
      </span>
      ),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        [10]
       </a>
      </sup>
      is a
      <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">
       landlocked country
      </a>
      in South Asia with a population of 26.4 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pre-cen_5-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-pre-cen-5">
        [5]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is a
      <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Nepal" title="Demographics of Nepal">
       multiethnic
      </a>
      nation with
      <a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">
       Nepali
      </a>
      as the official language.
      <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu" title="Kathmandu">
       Kathmandu
      </a>
      is the nation's capital and largest city. Modern Nepal is a
      <a href="/wiki/Secularism" title="Secularism">
       secular
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">
       parliamentary republic
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Nepal is bordered by
      <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">
       China
      </a>
      to the north and
      <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">
       India
      </a>
      to the south, east, and west. It is separated from
      <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">
       Bangladesh
      </a>
      by a narrow Indian corridor and from
      <a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">
       Bhutan
      </a>
      by the Indian state of
      <a href="/wiki/Sikkim" title="Sikkim">
       Sikkim
      </a>
      . Nepal is located in the
      <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">
       Himalayas
      </a>
      and is home to eight of the world's ten
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest_mountains#List" title="List of highest mountains">
       tallest mountains
      </a>
      , including
      <a href="/wiki/Mount_Everest" title="Mount Everest">
       Mount Everest
      </a>
      , the highest point on Earth. Its southern
      <a href="/wiki/Madhesh" title="Madhesh">
       Madhesh
      </a>
      region is fertile and humid.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        [11]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The country has an area of 147,181 square kilometres (56,827 sq mi), making it the world's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_total_area" title="List of countries and outlying territories by total area">
       93rd largest
      </a>
      country by area.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        [12]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is also the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population" title="List of countries by population">
       41st most populous
      </a>
      country.
     </p>
     <p>
      Nepal has a diverse ancient
      <a href="/wiki/Cultural_heritage" title="Cultural heritage">
       cultural heritage
      </a>
      . The name
      <i>
       Nepal
      </i>
      is first recorded in texts from the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vedic_Age" title="Vedic Age">
       Vedic Age
      </a>
      , the era that founded
      <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">
       Hinduism
      </a>
      , the country's predominant religion. Nepal was the world's last Hindu monarchy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        [13]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siddharta_Gautama" title="Siddharta Gautama">
       Siddharta Gautama
      </a>
      , the founder of
      <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
       Buddhism
      </a>
      , was born in
      <a href="/wiki/Lumbini" title="Lumbini">
       Lumbini
      </a>
      in southern Nepal. The main minorities are
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tibetan_Buddhists" title="Tibetan Buddhists">
       Tibetan Buddhists
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">
       Muslims
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kirant_Mundhum" title="Kirant Mundhum">
       Kiratans
      </a>
      , and Christians. The Nepalese are also known as
      <a href="/wiki/Gurkha" title="Gurkha">
       Gurkhas
      </a>
      . They have been reputed for their valour in
      <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
       World War I
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
       World War II
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Established in the 18th century, the early modern
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Nepal" title="Kingdom of Nepal">
       Kingdom of Nepal
      </a>
      was led by the
      <a href="/wiki/Shah_dynasty" title="Shah dynasty">
       Shah dynasty
      </a>
      , after
      <a href="/wiki/Prithvi_Narayan_Shah" title="Prithvi Narayan Shah">
       Prithvi Narayan Shah
      </a>
      unified many principalities in the region. Nepal is one of the few Asian countries which was never colonized.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        [14]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        [15]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Following the
      <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Nepalese_War" title="Anglo-Nepalese War">
       Anglo-Nepalese War
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Sugauli" title="Treaty of Sugauli">
       Treaty of Sugauli
      </a>
      in 1816, Nepal became an ally of the
      <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">
       British Empire
      </a>
      . A
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiparty_democracy" title="Multiparty democracy">
       multiparty democracy
      </a>
      evolved from 1951 to 1960, when
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Mahendra" title="King Mahendra">
       King Mahendra
      </a>
      enacted the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Panchayat_(Nepal)" title="Panchayat (Nepal)">
        panchayat
       </a>
      </i>
      system. In 1990,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliamentary_government" title="Parliamentary government">
       parliamentary government
      </a>
      was restored by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Birendra" title="King Birendra">
       King Birendra
      </a>
      . Nepal faced a decade-long
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nepali_Civil_War" title="Nepali Civil War">
       Communist Maoist insurgency
      </a>
      and mass protests against the authoritarian
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Gyanendra" title="King Gyanendra">
       King Gyanendra
      </a>
      in 2005, which led to the abolition of the monarchy in 2008. Its
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2nd_Nepalese_Constituent_Assembly" title="2nd Nepalese Constituent Assembly">
       2nd constituent assembly
      </a>
      promulgated a
      <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Nepal" title="Constitution of Nepal">
       new constitution
      </a>
      in 2015. Today, the main political blocs in Nepal are communists, social democrats and Hindu nationalists.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Nepali government works in the framework of a
      <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">
       representative democracy
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/Nepalese_Federal_States" title="Nepalese Federal States">
       seven federal provinces
      </a>
      . Nepal is a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_nation" title="Developing nation">
       developing nation
      </a>
      , ranking
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">
       145th
      </a>
      on the
      <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">
       Human Development Index
      </a>
      (HDI) in 2014. The country struggles with the transition from a monarchy to a republic. It also suffers from high levels of
      <a href="/wiki/Hunger" title="Hunger">
       hunger
      </a>
      and poverty. Despite these challenges, Nepal is making steady progress, with the government declaring its commitment to elevate the nation from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Least_developed_country" title="Least developed country">
       least developed country
      </a>
      status in 2022.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        [16]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        [17]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Nepal has friendship treaties with India and the United Kingdom.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        [18]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is a founding member and hosts the permanent secretariat of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SAARC" title="SAARC">
       SAARC
      </a>
      . It is also a member of the United Nations and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BIMSTEC" title="BIMSTEC">
       BIMSTEC
      </a>
      . Nepal is strategically important due to its location between Asia's great powers, China and India. It is also important for its
      <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">
       hydropower
      </a>
      potential.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        [19]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
       Etymology
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Local legends have that a Hindu sage named "Ne" established himself in the valley of Kathmandu in prehistoric times and that the word "Nepal" came into existence as the place was protected ("pala" in
      <a href="/wiki/Pali" title="Pali">
       Pali
      </a>
      ) by the sage "Nemi". It is mentioned in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vedic" title="Vedic">
       Vedic
      </a>
      texts that this region was called Nepal centuries ago. According to the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Skanda_Purana" title="Skanda Purana">
        Skanda Purana
       </a>
      </i>
      , a
      <a href="/wiki/Rishi" title="Rishi">
       rishi
      </a>
      called "Nemi" used to live in the
      <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">
       Himalayas
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        [20]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the
      <i>
       Pashupati Purana
      </i>
      , he is mentioned as a saint and a protector.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        [21]
       </a>
      </sup>
      He is said to have practised
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tapasya" title="Tapasya">
       meditation
      </a>
      at the Bagmati and Kesavati rivers
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        [22]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and to have taught there.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_23-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-23">
        [23]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The name of the country is also identical in origin to the name of the
      <a href="/wiki/Newar_people" title="Newar people">
       Newar people
      </a>
      . The terms "Nepāl", "Newār", "Newāl" and "Nepār" are phonetically different forms of the same word, and instances of the various forms appear in texts in different times in history. Nepal is the learned
      <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">
       Sanskrit
      </a>
      form and Newar is the colloquial
      <a href="/wiki/Prakrit" title="Prakrit">
       Prakrit
      </a>
      form.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        [24]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A Sanskrit inscription dated 512 CE found in Tistung, a valley to the west of Kathmandu, contains the phrase "greetings to the Nepals" indicating that the term "Nepal" was used to refer to both the country and the people.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        [25]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        [26]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      It has been suggested that "Nepal" may be a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sanskritization" title="Sanskritization">
       Sanskritization
      </a>
      of "Newar", or "Newar" may be a later form of "Nepal".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        [27]
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to another explanation, the words "Newar" and "Newari" are
      <a href="/wiki/Vulgarism" title="Vulgarism">
       vulgarisms
      </a>
      arising from the mutation of P to V, and L to R.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        [28]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Nepal is likely singular for Nephilim (n'p'l נפל) which is ancient Semitic for protector. Sanskrit is formed from the Phœnician Alphabet i.e.: Canaanite Aleph-Bet.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Nepal" title="History of Nepal">
       History of Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lumbini_-_Excavated_Buildings,_Lumbini_(9241388221).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Lumbini_-_Excavated_Buildings%2C_Lumbini_%289241388221%29.jpg/220px-Lumbini_-_Excavated_Buildings%2C_Lumbini_%289241388221%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Lumbini_-_Excavated_Buildings%2C_Lumbini_%289241388221%29.jpg/330px-Lumbini_-_Excavated_Buildings%2C_Lumbini_%289241388221%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Lumbini_-_Excavated_Buildings%2C_Lumbini_%289241388221%29.jpg/440px-Lumbini_-_Excavated_Buildings%2C_Lumbini_%289241388221%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lumbini_-_Excavated_Buildings,_Lumbini_(9241388221).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Lumbini" title="Lumbini">
         Lumbini
        </a>
        , listed as the birthplace of
        <a href="/wiki/Gautama_Buddha" title="Gautama Buddha">
         Gautama Buddha
        </a>
        by the
        <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
         UNESCO World Heritage Convention
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient">
       Ancient
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">
       Neolithic
      </a>
      tools found in the
      <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu_Valley" title="Kathmandu Valley">
       Kathmandu Valley
      </a>
      indicate that people have been living in the Himalayan region for at least eleven thousand years.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        [29]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The oldest population layer is believed to be represented by the
      <a href="/wiki/Kusunda_people" title="Kusunda people">
       Kusunda people
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        [30]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Nepal is first mentioned in the late Vedic
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Pari%C5%9Bi%E1%B9%A3%E1%B9%ADa#Atharvaveda" title="Pariśiṣṭa">
        Atharvaveda Pariśiṣṭa
       </a>
      </i>
      as a place exporting
      <a href="/wiki/Blanket" title="Blanket">
       blankets
      </a>
      and in the post-Vedic
      <i>
       Atharvashirsha
      </i>
      <a href="/wiki/Upanishads" title="Upanishads">
       Upanishad
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-31">
        [31]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Samudragupta" title="Samudragupta">
       Samudragupta
      </a>
      's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allahabad_Pillar" title="Allahabad Pillar">
       Allahabad Pillar
      </a>
      it is mentioned as a bordering country. The
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Skanda_Purana" title="Skanda Purana">
        Skanda Purana
       </a>
      </i>
      has a separate chapter known as "Nepal Mahatmya" that explains in more details about the beauty and power of Nepal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        [32]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nepal is also mentioned in
      <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">
       Hindu
      </a>
      texts such as the
      <i>
       Narayana Puja
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_31-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-31">
        [31]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Tibeto-Burman_languages" title="Tibeto-Burman languages">
       Tibeto-Burman-speaking
      </a>
      people probably lived in Nepal 2500 years ago.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Library_of_Congress_33-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Library_of_Congress-33">
        [33]
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, there is no archaeologic evidence of the
      <a href="/wiki/Gopal_Bansa" title="Gopal Bansa">
       Gopal Bansa
      </a>
      or Kirati rulers, only mention by the later
      <a href="/wiki/Licchavi_(kingdom)" title="Licchavi (kingdom)">
       Licchavi
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Malla_(Nepal)" title="Malla (Nepal)">
       Malla
      </a>
      eras.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        [34]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Around 500 BCE, small kingdoms and confederations of clans arose in the southern regions of Nepal. From one of these, the
      <a href="/wiki/Shakya" title="Shakya">
       Shakya
      </a>
      polity, arose a prince who later renounced his status to lead an ascetic life, founded
      <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
       Buddhism
      </a>
      , and came to be known as
      <a href="/wiki/Gautama_Buddha" title="Gautama Buddha">
       Gautama Buddha
      </a>
      (traditionally dated 563–483 BCE).
     </p>
     <p>
      By 250 BCE, the southern regions came under the influence of the
      <a href="/wiki/Maurya_Empire" title="Maurya Empire">
       Maurya Empire
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/North_India" title="North India">
       North India
      </a>
      and parts of Nepal later on became a nominal vassal state under the
      <a href="/wiki/Gupta_Empire" title="Gupta Empire">
       Gupta Empire
      </a>
      in the fourth century CE. Beginning in the third century CE, the
      <a href="/wiki/Licchavi_(kingdom)" title="Licchavi (kingdom)">
       Licchavi Kingdom
      </a>
      governed the
      <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu_Valley" title="Kathmandu Valley">
       Kathmandu Valley
      </a>
      and the region surrounding central Nepal.
     </p>
     <p>
      There is a quite detailed description of the kingdom of Nepal in the account of the renowned Chinese Buddhist pilgrim monk
      <a href="/wiki/Xuanzang" title="Xuanzang">
       Xuanzang
      </a>
      , dating from
      <i>
       c
      </i>
      . 645 CE.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        [35]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        [36]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Stone_inscriptions_in_the_Kathmandu_Valley" title="Stone inscriptions in the Kathmandu Valley">
       Stone inscriptions in the Kathmandu Valley
      </a>
      are important sources for the history of Nepal.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Licchavi dynasty went into decline in the late eighth century, probably due to the
      <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Empire" title="Tibetan Empire">
       Tibetan Empire
      </a>
      , and was followed by a
      <a href="/wiki/Newar_people" title="Newar people">
       Newar
      </a>
      or Thakuri era, from 879 CE (
      <a href="/wiki/Nepal_Sambat" title="Nepal Sambat">
       Nepal Sambat
      </a>
      1), although the extent of their control over the present-day country is uncertain.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        [37]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the eleventh century it seems to have included the
      <a href="/wiki/Pokhara" title="Pokhara">
       Pokhara
      </a>
      area. By the late eleventh century, southern Nepal came under the influence of the
      <a href="/wiki/Chalukya_dynasty" title="Chalukya dynasty">
       Chalukya dynasty
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/South_India" title="South India">
       South India
      </a>
      . Under the Chalukyas, Nepal's religious establishment changed as the kings patronised
      <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">
       Hinduism
      </a>
      instead of the Buddhism prevailing at that time.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval">
       Medieval
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Malla_(Nepal)" title="Malla (Nepal)">
       Malla (Nepal)
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Basantapurpalace.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Basantapurpalace.JPG/220px-Basantapurpalace.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Basantapurpalace.JPG/330px-Basantapurpalace.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Basantapurpalace.JPG/440px-Basantapurpalace.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Basantapurpalace.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Former royal palace at
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basantapur,_Kathmandu" title="Basantapur, Kathmandu">
         Basantapur, Kathmandu
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the early 12th century, leaders emerged in far western Nepal whose names ended with the Sanskrit suffix
      <i>
       malla
      </i>
      ("wrestler"). These kings consolidated their power and ruled over the next 200 years, until the kingdom splintered into two dozen petty states. Another Malla dynasty beginning with
      <a href="/wiki/Jayasthitimalla" title="Jayasthitimalla">
       Jayasthiti
      </a>
      emerged in the Kathmandu valley in the late 14th century, and much of central Nepal again came under a unified rule. In 1482 the realm was divided into three kingdoms:
      <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu" title="Kathmandu">
       Kathmandu
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patan,_Nepal" title="Patan, Nepal">
       Patan
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Bhaktapur" title="Bhaktapur">
       Bhaktapur
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Nepal_.281768.E2.80.932008.29">
       Kingdom of Nepal (1768–2008)
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Nepal" title="Kingdom of Nepal">
       Kingdom of Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Capture_of_Xiebulu.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1037" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Capture_of_Xiebulu.jpg/220px-Capture_of_Xiebulu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Capture_of_Xiebulu.jpg/330px-Capture_of_Xiebulu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Capture_of_Xiebulu.jpg/440px-Capture_of_Xiebulu.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Capture_of_Xiebulu.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Sino-Nepalese_War" title="Sino-Nepalese War">
         Sino-Nepalese War
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RaniOfNepal1920.jpg">

       </a>

        The Nepali queen and her ladies in the 1920s
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Samsad_Bhawan_02.jpg">

       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">

        The Old Parliament Building in
        <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu" title="Kathmandu">
         Kathmandu
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Presley_%26_Mahendra_(1).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="471" data-file-width="623" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Presley_%26_Mahendra_%281%29.jpg/220px-Presley_%26_Mahendra_%281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Presley_%26_Mahendra_%281%29.jpg/330px-Presley_%26_Mahendra_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Presley_%26_Mahendra_%281%29.jpg/440px-Presley_%26_Mahendra_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Presley_%26_Mahendra_(1).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">
         Elvis Presley
        </a>
        with
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Mahendra" title="King Mahendra">
         King Mahendra
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Ratna" title="Queen Ratna">
         Queen Ratna
        </a>
        of Nepal in 1960
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hillary_and_tenzing.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="494" data-file-width="828" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Hillary_and_tenzing.jpg/250px-Hillary_and_tenzing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Hillary_and_tenzing.jpg/375px-Hillary_and_tenzing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Hillary_and_tenzing.jpg/500px-Hillary_and_tenzing.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hillary_and_tenzing.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Hillary" title="Edmund Hillary">
         Edmund Hillary
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Tenzing_Norgay" title="Tenzing Norgay">
         Tenzing Norgay
        </a>
        became the first persons to summit
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mt_Everest" title="Mt Everest">
         Mt Everest
        </a>
        in Nepal in 1953
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bishweshwar_Prasad_Koirala_-_David_Ben_Gurion_1960.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="436" data-file-width="292" height="328" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Bishweshwar_Prasad_Koirala_-_David_Ben_Gurion_1960.jpg/220px-Bishweshwar_Prasad_Koirala_-_David_Ben_Gurion_1960.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8a/Bishweshwar_Prasad_Koirala_-_David_Ben_Gurion_1960.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bishweshwar_Prasad_Koirala_-_David_Ben_Gurion_1960.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Israeli leader
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/David_Ben_Gurion" title="David Ben Gurion">
         David Ben Gurion
        </a>
        and Prime Minister
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B._P._Koirala" title="B. P. Koirala">
         B. P. Koirala
        </a>
        (right), leader of the
        <a href="/wiki/Nepali_Congress" title="Nepali Congress">
         Nepali Congress
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the mid-18th century,
      <a href="/wiki/Prithvi_Narayan_Shah" title="Prithvi Narayan Shah">
       Prithvi Narayan Shah
      </a>
      , a
      <a href="/wiki/Gurkha" title="Gurkha">
       Gorkha
      </a>
      king, set out to put together what would become present-day Nepal. He embarked on his mission by securing the neutrality of the bordering mountain kingdoms. After several bloody battles and sieges, notably the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kirtipur" title="Battle of Kirtipur">
       Battle of Kirtipur
      </a>
      , he managed to conquer the Kathmandu Valley in 1769. A detailed account of Prithvi Narayan Shah's victory was written by Father Giuseppe, an eyewitness to the war.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        [38]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Gorkha dominion reached its height when the North Indian territories of the
      <a href="/wiki/Kumaon_Kingdom" title="Kumaon Kingdom">
       Kumaon
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Garhwal_Kingdom" title="Garhwal Kingdom">
       Garhwal Kingdoms
      </a>
      in the west to
      <a href="/wiki/Sikkim" title="Sikkim">
       Sikkim
      </a>
      in the east came under Nepal rule. At its maximum extent,
      <a href="/wiki/Greater_Nepal" title="Greater Nepal">
       Greater Nepal
      </a>
      extended from the
      <a href="/wiki/Teesta_River" title="Teesta River">
       Teesta River
      </a>
      in the east, to
      <a href="/wiki/Kangra,_Himachal_Pradesh" title="Kangra, Himachal Pradesh">
       Kangra, Himachal Pradesh
      </a>
      , across the
      <a href="/wiki/Sutlej" title="Sutlej">
       Sutlej
      </a>
      in the west as well as further south into the Terai plains and north of the Himalayas than at present. A dispute with
      <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">
       Tibet
      </a>
      over the control of mountain passes and inner Tingri valleys of Tibet forced the
      <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">
       Qing Emperor
      </a>
      of China to start the
      <a href="/wiki/Sino-Nepalese_War" title="Sino-Nepalese War">
       Sino-Nepali War
      </a>
      compelling the Nepali to retreat and pay heavy reparations to Peking.
     </p>
     <p>
      Rivalry between Kingdom of Nepal and the
      <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">
       East India Company
      </a>
      over the annexation of minor states bordering Nepal eventually led to the
      <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Nepalese_War" title="Anglo-Nepalese War">
       Anglo-Nepali War
      </a>
      (1815–16). At first the British underestimated the Nepali and were soundly defeated until committing more military resources than they had anticipated needing. They were greatly impressed by the valour and competence of their adversaries. Thus began the reputation of
      <a href="/wiki/Gurkha" title="Gurkha">
       Gurkhas
      </a>
      as fierce and ruthless soldiers. The war ended in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugauli_Treaty" title="Sugauli Treaty">
       Sugauli Treaty
      </a>
      , under which Nepal ceded recently captured portions of Sikkim and lands in Terai as well as the right to recruit soldiers.
      <a href="/wiki/Madhesi_people" title="Madhesi people">
       Madhesis
      </a>
      , having supported the East India Company during the war, had their lands gifted to Nepali.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_39-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-auto-39">
        [39]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Factionalism inside the royal family led to a period of instability. In 1846 a plot was discovered revealing that the reigning queen had planned to overthrow Jung Bahadur Kunwar, a fast-rising military leader. This led to the
      <a href="/wiki/Kot_massacre" title="Kot massacre">
       Kot massacre
      </a>
      ; armed clashes between military personnel and administrators loyal to the queen led to the execution of several hundred princes and chieftains around the country. Jung Bahadur Kunwar emerged victorious and founded the
      <a href="/wiki/Rana_dynasty" title="Rana dynasty">
       Rana dynasty
      </a>
      , later known as
      <a href="/wiki/Jung_Bahadur_Rana" title="Jung Bahadur Rana">
       Jung Bahadur Rana
      </a>
      . The king was made a titular figure, and the post of Prime Minister was made powerful and hereditary. The Ranas were staunchly pro-British and assisted them during the
      <a href="/wiki/Indian_Rebellion_of_1857" title="Indian Rebellion of 1857">
       Indian Rebellion of 1857
      </a>
      (and later in both World Wars). Some parts of the Terai region populated with non-Nepali peoples were gifted to Nepal by the British as a friendly gesture because of her military help to sustain British control in India during the rebellion. In 1923, the United Kingdom and Nepal formally signed an agreement of friendship that superseded the Sugauli Treaty of 1816.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_39-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-auto-39">
        [39]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_slavery_in_Asia" title="History of slavery in Asia">
       Slavery
      </a>
      was abolished in Nepal in 1924.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        [40]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nevertheless, debt bondage even involving debtors' children has been a persistent social problem in the Terai. Rana rule was marked by tyranny,
      <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/debauchery" title="wikt:debauchery">
       debauchery
      </a>
      , economic exploitation and religious persecution.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        [41]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        [42]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the late 1940s, newly emerging pro-democracy movements and political parties in Nepal were critical of the Rana autocracy. Meanwhile, with the invasion of Tibet by China in the 1950s, India sought to counterbalance the perceived military threat from its northern neighbour by taking pre-emptive steps to assert more influence in Nepal. India sponsored both
      <a href="/wiki/Tribhuvan_of_Nepal" title="Tribhuvan of Nepal">
       King Tribhuvan
      </a>
      (ruled 1911–55) as Nepal's new ruler in 1951 and a new government, mostly comprising the
      <a href="/wiki/Nepali_Congress" title="Nepali Congress">
       Nepali Congress
      </a>
      , thus terminating Rana hegemony in the kingdom.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_39-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-auto-39">
        [39]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After years of power wrangling between the king and the government,
      <a href="/wiki/Mahendra_of_Nepal" title="Mahendra of Nepal">
       King Mahendra
      </a>
      (ruled 1955–72) scrapped the democratic experiment in 1959, and a "partyless"
      <a href="/wiki/Panchayat_(Nepal)" title="Panchayat (Nepal)">
       Panchayat
      </a>
      system was made to govern Nepal until 1989, when the "Jan Andolan" (People's Movement) forced
      <a href="/wiki/Birendra_of_Nepal" title="Birendra of Nepal">
       King Birendra
      </a>
      (ruled 1972–2001) to accept constitutional reforms and to establish a multiparty parliament that took seat in May 1991.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nepal_Timeline_43-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Nepal_Timeline-43">
        [43]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1991–92, Bhutan expelled roughly 100,000 Bhutanese citizens of Nepali descent, most of whom have been living in seven refugee camps in eastern Nepal ever since.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bhutan_44-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bhutan-44">
        [44]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1996, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unified_Communist_Party_of_Nepal_(Maoist)" title="Unified Communist Party of Nepal (Maoist)">
       Communist Party of Nepal
      </a>
      started a bid to replace the royal parliamentary system with a people's republic by violent means. This led to the long
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nepali_Civil_War" title="Nepali Civil War">
       Nepali Civil War
      </a>
      and more than 12,000 deaths.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 1 June 2001, there was a
      <a href="/wiki/Nepalese_royal_massacre" title="Nepalese royal massacre">
       massacre in the royal palace
      </a>
      . King Birendra, Queen
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aishwarya_of_Nepal" title="Aishwarya of Nepal">
       Aishwarya
      </a>
      and seven other members of the royal family were killed. The perpetrator was
      <a href="/wiki/Dipendra_of_Nepal" title="Dipendra of Nepal">
       Crown Prince Dipendra
      </a>
      , who committed suicide (he died three days later) shortly thereafter. This outburst was alleged to have been Dipendra's response to his parents' refusal to accept his choice of wife. Nevertheless, there is speculation and doubts among Nepali citizens about who was responsible.
     </p>
     <p>
      Following the carnage, King Birendra's brother
      <a href="/wiki/Gyanendra_of_Nepal" title="Gyanendra of Nepal">
       Gyanendra
      </a>
      inherited the throne. On 1 February 2005, King Gyanendra dismissed the entire government and assumed full executive powers to quash the violent Maoist movement,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nepal_Timeline_43-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Nepal_Timeline-43">
        [43]
       </a>
      </sup>
      but this initiative was unsuccessful because a stalemate had developed in which the Maoists were firmly entrenched in large expanses of countryside but could not yet dislodge the military from numerous towns and the largest cities. In September 2005, the Maoists declared a three-month unilateral ceasefire to negotiate.
     </p>
     <p>
      In response to the
      <a href="/wiki/2006_democracy_movement_in_Nepal" title="2006 democracy movement in Nepal">
       2006 democracy movement
      </a>
      , King Gyanendra agreed to relinquish sovereign power to the people. On 24 April 2006 the dissolved House of Representatives was reinstated. Using its newly acquired sovereign authority, on 18 May 2006 the House of Representatives unanimously voted to curtail the power of the king and declared Nepal a
      <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">
       secular state
      </a>
      , ending its time-honoured official status as a Hindu Kingdom. On 28 December 2007, a bill was passed in parliament to amend Article 159 of the constitution – replacing "Provisions regarding the King" by "Provisions of the Head of the State" – declaring Nepal a
      <a href="/wiki/Federal_republic" title="Federal republic">
       federal republic
      </a>
      , and thereby abolishing the monarchy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_45-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CNN-45">
        [45]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The bill came into force on 28 May 2008.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abolish_46-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Abolish-46">
        [46]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_.282008.29">
       Republic (2008)
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unified_Communist_Party_of_Nepal_(Maoist)" title="Unified Communist Party of Nepal (Maoist)">
       Unified Communist Party of Nepal (Maoist)
      </a>
      won the largest number of seats in the
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nepali_Constituent_Assembly_election,_2008&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nepali Constituent Assembly election, 2008 (page does not exist)">
       Constituent Assembly election
      </a>
      held on 10 April 2008, and formed a coalition government which included most of the parties in the CA. Although acts of violence occurred during the pre-electoral period, election observers noted that the elections themselves were markedly peaceful and "well-carried out".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCC_47-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-TCC-47">
        [47]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dr._Ram_Baran_Yadav.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="736" data-file-width="745" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Dr._Ram_Baran_Yadav.jpg/220px-Dr._Ram_Baran_Yadav.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Dr._Ram_Baran_Yadav.jpg/330px-Dr._Ram_Baran_Yadav.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Dr._Ram_Baran_Yadav.jpg/440px-Dr._Ram_Baran_Yadav.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dr._Ram_Baran_Yadav.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Dr.
        <a href="/wiki/Ram_Baran_Yadav" title="Ram Baran Yadav">
         Ram Baran Yadav
        </a>
        , the first
        <a href="/wiki/President_of_Nepal" title="President of Nepal">
         President of Nepal
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The newly elected Assembly met in Kathmandu on 28 May 2008, and, after a polling of 564 constituent Assembly members, 560 voted to form a new government,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abolish_46-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Abolish-46">
        [46]
       </a>
      </sup>
      with the monarchist
      <a href="/wiki/Rastriya_Prajatantra_Party" title="Rastriya Prajatantra Party">
       Rastriya Prajatantra Party
      </a>
      , which had four members in the assembly, registering a dissenting note. At that point, it was declared that Nepal had become a secular and inclusive democratic republic,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        [48]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ekantipur_49-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Ekantipur-49">
        [49]
       </a>
      </sup>
      with the government announcing a three-day public holiday from 28–30 May. The king was thereafter given 15 days to vacate
      <a href="/wiki/Narayanhity_Palace" title="Narayanhity Palace">
       Narayanhity Palace
      </a>
      so it could reopen as a public museum.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        [50]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Nonetheless, political tensions and consequent power-sharing battles have continued in Nepal. In May 2009, the Maoist-led government was toppled and another coalition government with all major political parties barring the Maoists was formed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        [51]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Madhav_Kumar_Nepal" title="Madhav Kumar Nepal">
       Madhav Kumar Nepal
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Nepal_(Unified_Marxist%E2%80%93Leninist)" title="Communist Party of Nepal (Unified Marxist–Leninist)">
       Communist Party of Nepal (Unified Marxist–Leninist)
      </a>
      was made the Prime Minister of the coalition government.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        [52]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In February 2011 the Madhav Kumar Nepal Government was toppled and
      <a href="/wiki/Jhala_Nath_Khanal" title="Jhala Nath Khanal">
       Jhala Nath Khanal
      </a>
      of the Communist Party of Nepal (Unified Marxist–Leninist) was made the Prime Minister.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC:_South_Asia_53-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBC:_South_Asia-53">
        [53]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In August 2011 the Jhala Nath Khanal Government was toppled and
      <a href="/wiki/Baburam_Bhattarai" title="Baburam Bhattarai">
       Baburam Bhattarai
      </a>
      of the Communist Party of Nepal (Maoist) was made the Prime Minister.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        [54]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The political parties were unable to draft a constitution in the stipulated time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jagaran_Nepal_55-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jagaran_Nepal-55">
        [55]
       </a>
      </sup>
      This led to dissolution of the Constituent Assembly to pave way for new elections to strive for a new political mandate. In opposition to the theory of
      <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">
       separation of powers
      </a>
      , then Chief Justice Khil Raj Regmi was made the chairman of the
      <a href="/wiki/Caretaker_government" title="Caretaker government">
       caretaker government
      </a>
      . Under Regmi, the nation saw peaceful elections for the constituent assembly. The major forces in the earlier constituent assembly (namely CPN Maoists and Madhesi parties) dropped to distant 3rd and even below.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Official_page_of_Constituent_Assembly_of_Nepal_56-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Official_page_of_Constituent_Assembly_of_Nepal-56">
        [56]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter_Center_publication_on_Nepal_Peace_Reports_57-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Carter_Center_publication_on_Nepal_Peace_Reports-57">
        [57]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In February 2014, after consensus was reached between the two major parties in the constituent assembly, Sushil Koirala was sworn in as the new prime minister of Nepal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_58-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBC-58">
        [58]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kantipur_Publications_59-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Kantipur_Publications-59">
        [59]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 20 September 2015, a new constitution, the "
      <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Nepal" title="Constitution of Nepal">
       Constitution of Nepal
      </a>
      2015"
      <small>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">
        Nepali
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="ne">
        नेपालको संविधान २०७२
       </span>
       )
      </small>
      was announced by President
      <a href="/wiki/Ram_Baran_Yadav" title="Ram Baran Yadav">
       Ram Baran Yadav
      </a>
      in the constituent assembly. The constituent assembly was transformed into a legislative parliament by the then-chairman of that assembly. The new constitution of Nepal has changed Nepal practically into a federal democratic republic by making 7 unnamed states.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 25 April 2015,
      <a href="/wiki/April_2015_Nepal_earthquake" title="April 2015 Nepal earthquake">
       a magnitude 7.8 earthquake
      </a>
      struck Nepal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        [60]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Two weeks later, on 12 May, another earthquake with a magnitude of 7.3 hit Nepal, which left more than 8,500 people dead and about 21,000, injured.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        [61]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In October 2015,
      <a href="/wiki/Bidhya_Devi_Bhandari" title="Bidhya Devi Bhandari">
       Bidhya Devi Bhandari
      </a>
      was nominated as the first female president.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        [62]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
       Geography
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Nepal" title="Geography of Nepal">
       Geography of Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Un-nepal.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2257" data-file-width="3038" height="334" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Un-nepal.png/450px-Un-nepal.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Un-nepal.png/675px-Un-nepal.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Un-nepal.png/900px-Un-nepal.png 2x" width="450"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Un-nepal.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A map of Nepal.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nepal_topo_en.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="852" data-file-width="1400" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Nepal_topo_en.jpg/450px-Nepal_topo_en.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Nepal_topo_en.jpg/675px-Nepal_topo_en.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Nepal_topo_en.jpg/900px-Nepal_topo_en.jpg 2x" width="450"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nepal_topo_en.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A topographic map of Nepal.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nepal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1130" data-file-width="1900" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Nepal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/300px-Nepal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Nepal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/450px-Nepal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Nepal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/600px-Nepal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nepal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Nepal map of Köppen climate classification.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Nepal is of roughly trapezoidal shape, 800 kilometres (497 mi) long and 200 kilometres (124 mi) wide, with an area of 147,181 km
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      (56,827 sq mi). See
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_and_geographic_subdivisions_by_total_area_from_100,000_to_1,000,000_km%C2%B2" title="List of political and geographic subdivisions by total area from 100,000 to 1,000,000 km²">
       List of territories by size
      </a>
      for the comparative size of Nepal. It lies between latitudes
      <a href="/wiki/26th_parallel_north" title="26th parallel north">
       26°
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/31st_parallel_north" title="31st parallel north">
       31°N
      </a>
      , and longitudes
      <a href="/wiki/80th_meridian_east" title="80th meridian east">
       80°
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/89th_meridian_east" title="89th meridian east">
       89°E
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Nepal is commonly divided into three physiographic areas: Mountain,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hill_Region" title="Hill Region">
       Hill
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Terai" title="Terai">
       Terai
      </a>
      . These ecological belts run east-west and are vertically intersected by Nepal's major, north to south flowing river systems.
     </p>
     <p>
      The southern lowland plains or
      <i>
       Terai
      </i>
      bordering India are part of the northern rim of the
      <a href="/wiki/Indo-Gangetic_Plain" title="Indo-Gangetic Plain">
       Indo-Gangetic Plain
      </a>
      . They were formed and are fed by three major Himalayan rivers: the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Koshi_river" title="Koshi river">
       Kosi
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Gandaki_River" title="Gandaki River">
       Narayani
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/Ghaghara" title="Ghaghara">
       Karnali
      </a>
      as well as smaller rivers rising below the permanent snowline. This region has a subtropical to tropical climate. The outermost range of foothills called
      <a href="/wiki/Sivalik_Hills" title="Sivalik Hills">
       Sivalik Hills
      </a>
      or Churia Range cresting at 700 to 1,000 metres (2,297 to 3,281 ft) marks the limit of the Gangetic Plain, however broad, low valleys called
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inner_Terai_Valleys_of_Nepal" title="Inner Terai Valleys of Nepal">
       Inner Tarai Valleys
      </a>
      (Bhitri Tarai Uptyaka) lie north of these foothills in several places.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Hill Region (
      <i>
       Pahad
      </i>
      ) abuts the mountains and varies from 800 to 4,000 metres (2,625 to 13,123 ft) in altitude with progression from subtropical climates below 1,200 metres (3,937 ft) to alpine climates above 3,600 metres (11,811 ft). The
      <a href="/wiki/Lower_Himalayan_Range" title="Lower Himalayan Range">
       Lower Himalayan Range
      </a>
      reaching 1,500 to 3,000 metres (4,921 to 9,843 ft) is the southern limit of this region, with subtropical river valleys and "hills" alternating to the north of this range. Population density is high in valleys but notably less above 2,000 metres (6,562 ft) and very low above 2,500 metres (8,202 ft) where snow occasionally falls in winter.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Mountain Region (
      <i>
       Himal
      </i>
      ), situated in the Great Himalayan Range, makes up the northern part of Nepal. It contains the highest elevations in the world including 8,848 metres (29,029 ft) height
      <a href="/wiki/Mount_Everest" title="Mount Everest">
       Mount Everest
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       Sagarmāthā
      </i>
      in Nepali) on the border with China. Seven other of the world's "
      <a href="/wiki/Eight-thousander" title="Eight-thousander">
       eight-thousanders
      </a>
      " are in Nepal or on its border with China:
      <a href="/wiki/Lhotse" title="Lhotse">
       Lhotse
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Makalu" title="Makalu">
       Makalu
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Cho_Oyu" title="Cho Oyu">
       Cho Oyu
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kangchenjunga" title="Kangchenjunga">
       Kangchenjunga
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Dhaulagiri" title="Dhaulagiri">
       Dhaulagiri
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annapurna" title="Annapurna">
       Annapurna
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Manaslu" title="Manaslu">
       Manaslu
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
       Climate
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Nepal has five climatic zones, broadly corresponding to the altitudes. The tropical and subtropical zones lie below 1,200 metres (3,937 ft), the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperate" title="Temperate">
       temperate
      </a>
      zone 1,200 to 2,400 metres (3,937 to 7,874 ft), the cold zone 2,400 to 3,600 metres (7,874 to 11,811 ft), the subarctic zone 3,600 to 4,400 metres (11,811 to 14,436 ft), and the Arctic zone above 4,400 metres (14,436 ft).
     </p>
     <p>
      Nepal experiences five seasons: summer,
      <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">
       monsoon
      </a>
      , autumn, winter and spring. The Himalaya blocks cold winds from Central Asia in the winter and forms the northern limit of the monsoon wind patterns. In a land once thickly forested,
      <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Nepal" title="Deforestation in Nepal">
       deforestation
      </a>
      is a major problem in all regions, with resulting erosion and degradation of ecosystems.
     </p>
     <p>
      Nepal is popular for mountaineering, having some of the highest and most challenging mountains in the world, including
      <a href="/wiki/Mount_Everest" title="Mount Everest">
       Mount Everest
      </a>
      . Technically, the south-east ridge on the Nepali side of the mountain is easier to climb; so, most climbers prefer to trek to Everest through Nepal.
     </p>
     <p>
      The highest mountains in Nepal are given here:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        [63]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

       </td>

       </td>
       <td style="text-align:center; background:rgb(143, 177, 172);">
        26,906 ft
       </td>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">
       Geology
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Nepal" title="Geology of Nepal">
       Geology of Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The collision between the
      <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">
       Indian subcontinent
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">
       Eurasia
      </a>
      , which started in
      <a href="/wiki/Paleogene" title="Paleogene">
       Paleogene
      </a>
      time and continues today, produced the Himalaya and the
      <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Plateau" title="Tibetan Plateau">
       Tibetan Plateau
      </a>
      . Nepal lies completely within this collision zone, occupying the central sector of the Himalayan arc, nearly one third of the 2,400 km (1,500 mi)-long Himalayas.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        [64]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        [65]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        [66]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        [67]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        [68]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        [69]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Indian plate continues to move north relative to Asia at the rate of approximately 50 mm (2.0 in) per year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        [70]
       </a>
      </sup>
      This is approximately twice the speed at which human fingernails grow, which is very fast given the size of the blocks of Earth's crust involved.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research">
         <span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (September 2015)">
          original research?
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      As the strong Indian continental crust subducts beneath the relatively weak Tibetan crust, it pushes up the Himalayan Mountains. This collision zone has accommodated huge amounts of crustal shortening as the rock sequences slide one over another.
     </p>
     <p>
      Based on a study published in 2014, of the Main Frontal Thrust, on average a great earthquake occurs every 750 ± 140 and 870 ± 350 years in the east Nepal region.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        [71]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A study from 2015 found a 700-year delay between earthquakes in the region. The study also suggests, that because of tectonic stress transfer,
      <a href="/wiki/1934_Nepal%E2%80%93Bihar_earthquake" title="1934 Nepal–Bihar earthquake">
       the earthquake from 1934 in Nepal
      </a>
      and the 2015 earthquake are connected - following a historic earthquake pattern.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        [72]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Erosion of the Himalayas is a very important source of sediment, which flows via several great rivers: the
      <a href="/wiki/Indus_River" title="Indus River">
       Indus
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ganges" title="Ganges">
       Ganges
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Brahmaputra_River" title="Brahmaputra River">
       Brahmaputra River
      </a>
      systems to the Indian Ocean.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        [73]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">
       Environment
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The dramatic differences in elevation found in Nepal result in a variety of
      <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">
       biomes
      </a>
      , from
      <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_grasslands,_savannas,_and_shrublands" title="Tropical and subtropical grasslands, savannas, and shrublands">
       tropical savannas
      </a>
      along the Indian border, to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical" title="Subtropical">
       subtropical
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_moist_broadleaf_forests" title="Tropical and subtropical moist broadleaf forests">
       broadleaf
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_coniferous_forests" title="Tropical and subtropical coniferous forests">
       coniferous forests
      </a>
      in the Hill Region, to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperate" title="Temperate">
       temperate
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_and_mixed_forests" title="Temperate broadleaf and mixed forests">
       broadleaf
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Temperate_coniferous_forest" title="Temperate coniferous forest">
       coniferous
      </a>
      forests on the slopes of the Himalaya, to
      <a href="/wiki/Montane_grasslands_and_shrublands" title="Montane grasslands and shrublands">
       montane grasslands and shrublands
      </a>
      and rock and ice at the highest elevations.
     </p>
     <p>
      At the lowest elevations is the
      <a href="/wiki/Terai-Duar_savanna_and_grasslands" title="Terai-Duar savanna and grasslands">
       Terai-Duar savanna and grasslands
      </a>
      ecoregion. These form a mosaic with the
      <a href="/wiki/Himalayan_subtropical_broadleaf_forests" title="Himalayan subtropical broadleaf forests">
       Himalayan subtropical broadleaf forests
      </a>
      , which occur from 500 to 1,000 metres (1,600 to 3,300 ft) and include the Inner Terai Valleys.
      <a href="/wiki/Himalayan_subtropical_pine_forests" title="Himalayan subtropical pine forests">
       Himalayan subtropical pine forests
      </a>
      occur between 1,000 and 2,000 metres (3,300 and 6,600 ft).
     </p>
     <p>
      Above these elevations, the
      <a href="/wiki/Biogeography" title="Biogeography">
       biogeography
      </a>
      of Nepal is generally divided from east to west by the Gandaki River. Ecoregions to the east tend to receive more precipitation and to be more species-rich. Those to the west are drier with fewer species.
     </p>
     <p>
      From 1,500 to 3,000 metres (4,900 to 9,800 ft), are temperate broadleaf forests: the
      <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Himalayan_broadleaf_forests" title="Eastern Himalayan broadleaf forests">
       eastern
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Western_Himalayan_broadleaf_forests" title="Western Himalayan broadleaf forests">
       western Himalayan broadleaf forests
      </a>
      . From 3,000 to 4,000 metres (9,800 to 13,100 ft) are the
      <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Himalayan_subalpine_conifer_forests" title="Eastern Himalayan subalpine conifer forests">
       eastern
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Western_Himalayan_subalpine_conifer_forests" title="Western Himalayan subalpine conifer forests">
       western Himalayan subalpine conifer forests
      </a>
      . To 5,500 metres (18,000 ft) are the
      <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Himalayan_alpine_shrub_and_meadows" title="Eastern Himalayan alpine shrub and meadows">
       eastern
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Western_Himalayan_alpine_shrub_and_meadows" title="Western Himalayan alpine shrub and meadows">
       western Himalayan alpine shrub and meadows
      </a>
      .
     </p>

           <img alt="" data-file-height="1440" data-file-width="2560" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Hills_Views.jpg/320px-Hills_Views.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Hills_Views.jpg/480px-Hills_Views.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Hills_Views.jpg/640px-Hills_Views.jpg 2x" width="214"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>

          Hills view of Ghorahi, Dang
         </p>
        </div>
       </div>
      </li>
      <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 215.33333333333px">
       <div style="width: 215.33333333333px">
        <div class="thumb" style="width: 213.33333333333px;">
         <div style="margin:0px auto;">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:View_of_hills.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="1440" data-file-width="2560" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/View_of_hills.jpg/320px-View_of_hills.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/View_of_hills.jpg/480px-View_of_hills.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/View_of_hills.jpg/640px-View_of_hills.jpg 2x" width="214"/>
          </a>

        </div>
