         <p>
          View of mountains
         </p>
        </div>
       </div>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">
       Politics
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Nepal" title="Politics of Nepal">
       Politics of Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:left; float:right; margin-right:9px; margin-left:2px;">
      <tr>
       <td style="text-align;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bidya_bhandaRi.jpg">
         <img alt="Bidya bhandaRi.jpg" data-file-height="576" data-file-width="617" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Bidya_bhandaRi.jpg/120px-Bidya_bhandaRi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Bidya_bhandaRi.jpg/180px-Bidya_bhandaRi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Bidya_bhandaRi.jpg/240px-Bidya_bhandaRi.jpg 2x" width="120"/>
        </a>
       </td>
       <td style="text-align;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prachanda_2009.jpg">
         <img alt="Prachanda 2009.jpg" data-file-height="1417" data-file-width="1500" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Prachanda_2009.jpg/120px-Prachanda_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Prachanda_2009.jpg/180px-Prachanda_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Prachanda_2009.jpg/240px-Prachanda_2009.jpg 2x" width="120"/>
        </a>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td style="text-align:center;">
        <a href="/wiki/Bidhya_Devi_Bhandari" title="Bidhya Devi Bhandari">
         Bidhya Devi Bhandari
        </a>
        <br/>
        <small>
         <a href="/wiki/President_of_Nepal" title="President of Nepal">
          President
         </a>
         since 2015
        </small>
       </td>
       <td style="text-align:center;">
        <a href="/wiki/Pushpa_Kamal_Dahal" title="Pushpa Kamal Dahal">
         Pushpa Kamal Dahal
        </a>
        <br/>
        <small>
         <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Nepal" title="List of Prime Ministers of Nepal">
          Prime Minister
         </a>
         since 3 August 2016
        </small>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      Nepal has seen rapid political changes during the last two decades. Up until 1990, Nepal was a monarchy under executive control of the King. Faced with a communist movement against absolute monarchy,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Birendra" title="King Birendra">
       King Birendra
      </a>
      , in 1990, agreed to a large-scale political reform by creating a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliamentary_monarchy" title="Parliamentary monarchy">
       parliamentary monarchy
      </a>
      with the king as the
      <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">
       head of state
      </a>
      and a prime minister as the head of the government.
     </p>
     <p>
      Nepal's legislature was
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicameral" title="Bicameral">
       bicameral
      </a>
      , consisting of a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nepal_House_of_Representatives" title="Nepal House of Representatives">
       House of Representatives
      </a>
      called the Pratinidhi Sabha and a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Council_of_Nepal" title="National Council of Nepal">
       National Council
      </a>
      called the Rastriya Sabha. The House of Representatives consisted of 205 members directly elected by the people. The National Council had 60 members: ten nominated by the king, 35 elected by the House of Representatives, and the remaining 15 elected by an electoral college made up of chairs of villages and towns. The legislature had a five-year term but was dissolvable by the king before its term could end. All Nepali citizens 18 years and older became eligible to vote.
     </p>
     <p>
      The executive comprised the King and the Council of Ministers (the cabinet). The leader of the coalition or party securing the maximum seats in an election was appointed as the Prime Minister. The Cabinet was appointed by the king on the recommendation of the Prime Minister. Governments in Nepal tended to be highly unstable, falling either through internal collapse or parliamentary dissolution by the monarch, on the recommendation of the prime minister, according to the constitution; no government has survived for more than two years since 1991.
     </p>
     <p>
      The movement in April 2006 brought about a change in the nation's governance: an interim constitution was promulgated, with the King giving up power, and an interim House of Representatives was formed with Maoist members after the new government held peace talks with the Maoist rebels. The number of parliamentary seats was also increased to 330. In April 2007, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unified_Communist_Party_of_Nepal_(Maoist)" title="Unified Communist Party of Nepal (Maoist)">
       Communist Party of Nepal (Maoist)
      </a>
      joined the interim government of Nepal.
     </p>
     <p>
      In December 2007, the interim parliament passed a bill making Nepal a federal republic, with a president as head of state. Elections for the constitutional assembly were held on 10 April 2008; the Maoist party led the results but did not achieve a simple majority of seats.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        [74]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The new parliament adopted the 2007 bill at its first meeting by an overwhelming majority, and King
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gyanendra" title="Gyanendra">
       Gyanendra
      </a>
      was given 15 days to leave the Royal Palace in central Kathmandu. He left on 11 June.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Telegraph_75-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Telegraph-75">
        [75]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 26 June 2008, the prime minister
      <a href="/wiki/Girija_Prasad_Koirala" title="Girija Prasad Koirala">
       Girija Prasad Koirala
      </a>
      , who had served as Acting Head of State since January 2007, announced that he would resign on the election of the country's first president by the Constituent Assembly. The first round of voting, on 19 July 2008, saw
      <a href="/wiki/Parmanand_Jha" title="Parmanand Jha">
       Parmanand Jha
      </a>
      win election as Nepali vice-president, but neither of the contenders for president received the required 298 votes and a second round was held two days later.
      <a href="/wiki/Ram_Baran_Yadav" title="Ram Baran Yadav">
       Ram Baran Yadav
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Nepali_Congress" title="Nepali Congress">
       Nepali Congress
      </a>
      party defeated Maoist-backed
      <a href="/wiki/Ram_Raja_Prasad_Singh" title="Ram Raja Prasad Singh">
       Ram Raja Prasad Singh
      </a>
      with 308 of the 590 votes cast.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        [76]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Koirala submitted his resignation to the new president after Yadav's swearing-in ceremony on 23 July 2008.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 15 August 2008, Maoist leader
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prachanda" title="Prachanda">
       Prachanda
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Pushpa_Kamal_Dahal" title="Pushpa Kamal Dahal">
       Pushpa Kamal Dahal
      </a>
      ) was elected Prime Minister of Nepal, the first since the country's transition from a monarchy to a republic. On 4 May 2009, Dahal resigned over on-going conflicts with regard to the sacking of the Army chief. Since Dahal's resignation, the country has been in a serious political deadlock with one of the big issues being the proposed integration of the former Maoist combatants, also known as the People's Liberation Army, into the national security forces.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        [77]
       </a>
      </sup>
      After Dahal, Jhala Nath Khanal of CPN (UML) was elected the Prime Minister. Khanal was forced to step down as he could not succeed in carrying forward the Peace Process and the constitution writing. On August 2011, Maoist Babu Ram Bhattarai became third Prime Minister after the election of constituent assembly.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        [78]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 24 May 2012, Nepals's Deputy PM Krishna Sitaula resigned.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kantiput_79-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Kantiput-79">
        [79]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 27 May 2012, the country's Constituent Assembly failed to meet the deadline for writing a new constitution for the country. Prime Minister Baburam Bhattarai announced that new elections will be held on 22 November 2012. "We have no other option but to go back to the people and elect a new assembly to write the constitution," he said in a nationally televised speech. One of the main obstacles has been disagreement over whether the states which will be created will be based on ethnicity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        [80]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Nepal is one of the few countries in Asia to abolish the death penalty.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        [81]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nepal is the only Asian country where the possibility of
      <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">
       same-sex marriage
      </a>
      has been proposed in the high court and in the legislature although same-sex marriage currently does not exist in Nepal (see also
      <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Nepal" title="LGBT rights in Nepal">
       LGBT rights in Nepal
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Nepal" title="Same-sex marriage in Nepal">
       Same-sex marriage in Nepal
      </a>
      ). The decision was based on a seven-person government committee study, and enacted through
      <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Nepal" title="Supreme Court of Nepal">
       Supreme Court
      </a>
      's ruling November 2008. The ruling granted full rights for
      <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">
       LGBT
      </a>
      individuals, including the right to marry
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        [82]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and now can get
      <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">
       citizenship
      </a>
      as a
      <a href="/wiki/Third_gender" title="Third gender">
       third gender
      </a>
      rather than male or female as authorized by Nepal's Supreme Court in 2007.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        [83]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Constitution">
       Constitution
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Nepal is governed according to the
      <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Nepal" title="Constitution of Nepal">
       Constitution of Nepal
      </a>
      , which came into effect on 20 September 2015, replacing the Interim Constitution of 2007. The Constitution was drafted by the Second Constituent Assembly following the failure of the First Constituent Assembly to produce a constitution in its mandated period. The constitution is the fundamental law of Nepal. It defines Nepal as having multi-ethnic, multi-lingual, multi-religious, multi-cultural characteristics with common aspirations of people living in diverse geographical regions, and being committed to and united by a bond of allegiance to national independence, territorial integrity, national interest and prosperity of Nepal. All the Nepali people collectively constitute the nation.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Government">
       Government
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Simha_Durbar_Gate.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1392" data-file-width="2228" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Simha_Durbar_Gate.jpg/300px-Simha_Durbar_Gate.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Simha_Durbar_Gate.jpg/450px-Simha_Durbar_Gate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Simha_Durbar_Gate.jpg/600px-Simha_Durbar_Gate.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Simha_Durbar_Gate.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Entrance to
        <a href="/wiki/Singha_Durbar" title="Singha Durbar">
         Singha Durbar
        </a>
        , the seat of the Nepali government in Kathmandu
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Constitution of Nepal has defined three organs of the government.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        [84]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Executive">
       Executive
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The form of governance of Nepal shall be a multi-party, competitive, federal democratic republican parliamentary system based on plurality.
     </p>
     <h5>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_executive">
       Federal executive
      </span>
     </h5>
     <p>
      The executive power of Nepal shall rest with the Council of Ministers in accordance with the Constitution and law.The President shall appoint the parliamentary party leader of the political party with the majority in the House of Representatives as a Prime Minister, and a Council of Ministers shall be formed in his/her chairmanship
     </p>
     <h5>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Provincial_executive">
       Provincial executive
      </span>
     </h5>
     <p>
      The executive power of the Province shall, pursuant to the Constitution and laws, be vested in the Council of Ministers of the Province. Provided that the executive power of the Province shall be exercised by the Provincial Head in case of absence of the Provincial Executive in a State of Emergency or enforcement of Federal rule. Every province shall have a Provincial Head as the representative of the Federal government. The President shall appoint a Provincial Head for every province. The Provincial Head shall exercise the rights and duties as specified in the constitution or laws. The Provincial Head shall appoint the leader of the parliamentary party with majority in the Provincial Assembly as the Chief Minister and the Provincial Council of Ministers shall be formed under the chairpersonship of the Chief Minister.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Legislative">
       Legislative
      </span>
     </h4>
     <h5>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_legislature">
       Federal legislature
      </span>
     </h5>
     <p>
      There shall be a Legislature, called Federal Parliament, consisting of two Houses, namely the House of Representatives and the National Assembly.
     </p>
     <h6>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_House_of_Representatives">
       The House of Representatives
      </span>
     </h6>
     <p>
      Except when dissolved earlier, the term of House of Representatives shall be five years. The House of Representatives shall consist of 275 members as follows:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       165 members elected through the first-past-the-post electoral system consisting of one member from each of the one hundred and sixty five electoral constituencies formed by dividing Nepal into 165 constituencies based on geography, and population.
      </li>
      <li>
       110 elected from proportional representation electoral system where voters vote for parties, while treating the whole country as a single electoral constituency.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h6>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_National_Assembly">
       The National Assembly
      </span>
     </h6>
     <p>
      National Assembly shall be a permanent house. The tenure of members of National Assembly shall be six years. The National Assembly shall consist of two 59 members as follows:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       56 members elected from an Electoral College comprising members of Provincial Assembly and chairpersons and vice-chairpersons of Village councils and Mayors and Deputy Mayors of Municipal councils, with different weights of votes for each, with eight members from each province, including at least three women, one Dalit, one person with disability or minority;
      </li>
      <li>
       3 members, including at least one woman, to be nominated by the President on the recommendation of Government of Nepal.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h5>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Provincial_legislature">
       Provincial legislature
      </span>
     </h5>
     <p>
      There shall be a unicameral legislature in a province which shall be called the Provincial Assembly. Every Provincial Assembly shall consist of the following number of members:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Members equal to double the number of members to be elected through the first-past-the-post (FPTP) election system to the House of Representatives from the concerned province,
      </li>
      <li>
       The number of members to be elected through the Proportional Representation (PR) election system equal to the number equivalent to the remaining forty per cent when the number of members from FPTP is regarded as sixty per cent.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Judiciary">
       Judiciary
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Powers relating to justice in Nepal shall be exercised by courts and other judicial institutions in accordance with the provisions of this Constitution, other laws and recognized principles of justice. There shall be the following courts in Nepal:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Supreme Court
      </li>
      <li>
       High Courts
      </li>
      <li>
       District Courts
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">
       Foreign relations
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Nepal" title="Foreign relations of Nepal">
       Foreign relations of Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Embassy_of_Nepal.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2572" data-file-width="1607" height="352" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Embassy_of_Nepal.JPG/220px-Embassy_of_Nepal.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Embassy_of_Nepal.JPG/330px-Embassy_of_Nepal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Embassy_of_Nepal.JPG/440px-Embassy_of_Nepal.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Embassy_of_Nepal.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_Nepal_in_Washington,_D.C." title="Embassy of Nepal in Washington, D.C.">
         Embassy of Nepal in Washington, D.C.
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Nepal has close ties with both of its neighbors, India and China. In accordance with a long-standing treaty, Indian and Nepali citizens may travel to each other's countries without a passport or visa. Nepali citizens may work in India without legal restriction. The
      <a href="/wiki/Indian_Army" title="Indian Army">
       Indian Army
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Britain%E2%80%93India%E2%80%93Nepal_Tripartite_Agreement" title="Britain–India–Nepal Tripartite Agreement">
       maintains
      </a>
      seven
      <a href="/wiki/Gorkha_regiments_(India)" title="Gorkha regiments (India)">
       Gorkha regiments
      </a>
      consisting of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gorkha" title="Gorkha">
       Gorkha
      </a>
      troops recruited mostly from Nepal.
     </p>
     <p>
      However, in the years since the
      <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Nepal" title="Government of Nepal">
       Government of Nepal
      </a>
      has been dominated by socialists, and
      <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">
       India's government
      </a>
      has been controlled by more right-wing parties, India has been remilitarizing the "porous" Indo-Nepali border to stifle the flow of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamist" title="Islamist">
       Islamist
      </a>
      groups.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        [85]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Nepal established relations with the People's Republic of China on 1 August 1955, and relations since have been based on the
      <a href="/wiki/Five_Principles_of_Peaceful_Coexistence" title="Five Principles of Peaceful Coexistence">
       Five Principles of Peaceful Coexistence
      </a>
      . Nepal has aided China in the aftermath of the
      <a href="/wiki/2008_Sichuan_earthquake" title="2008 Sichuan earthquake">
       2008 Sichuan earthquake
      </a>
      , and China has provided economic assistance for Nepali infrastructure. Both countries have cooperated to host the
      <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics_summit_of_Mt._Everest" title="2008 Summer Olympics summit of Mt. Everest">
       2008 Summer Olympics summit of Mt. Everest
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        [86]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nepal has assisted in curbing anti-China protests from the
      <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_diaspora" title="Tibetan diaspora">
       Tibetan diaspora
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        [87]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Military">
       Military
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Nepalese_Armed_Forces" title="Nepalese Armed Forces">
       Nepalese Armed Forces
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gurkha_Memorial,_Horse_Guards_Avenue_-_geograph.org.uk_-_379881.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="480" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Gurkha_Memorial%2C_Horse_Guards_Avenue_-_geograph.org.uk_-_379881.jpg/220px-Gurkha_Memorial%2C_Horse_Guards_Avenue_-_geograph.org.uk_-_379881.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Gurkha_Memorial%2C_Horse_Guards_Avenue_-_geograph.org.uk_-_379881.jpg/330px-Gurkha_Memorial%2C_Horse_Guards_Avenue_-_geograph.org.uk_-_379881.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Gurkha_Memorial%2C_Horse_Guards_Avenue_-_geograph.org.uk_-_379881.jpg/440px-Gurkha_Memorial%2C_Horse_Guards_Avenue_-_geograph.org.uk_-_379881.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gurkha_Memorial,_Horse_Guards_Avenue_-_geograph.org.uk_-_379881.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Gurkha" title="Gurkha">
         Gurkha
        </a>
        Memorial, London
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Nepal's military consists of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nepal_Army" title="Nepal Army">
       Nepali Army
      </a>
      , which includes the
      <a href="/wiki/Nepalese_Army_Air_Service" title="Nepalese Army Air Service">
       Nepali Army Air Service
      </a>
      . The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nepalese_Police_Force" title="Nepalese Police Force">
       Nepali Police Force
      </a>
      is the civilian police and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armed_Police_Force_Nepal" title="Armed Police Force Nepal">
       Armed Police Force Nepal
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        [88]
       </a>
      </sup>
      is the paramilitary force. Service is voluntary and the minimum age for enlistment is 18 years. Nepal spends $99.2 million (2004) on its military—1.5% of its GDP. Much of the equipment and arms are imported from India. Consequently, the US provided M16s, M4s and other Colt weapons to combat communist (Maoist) insurgents. The standard-issue battle rifle of the Nepali army is the Colt M16.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        [89]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the new regulations by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nepal_Army" title="Nepal Army">
       Nepali Army
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Female_soldiers" title="Female soldiers">
       female soldiers
      </a>
      have been barred from participating in
      <a href="/wiki/Combat" title="Combat">
       combat
      </a>
      situations and fighting in the frontlines of war. However, they are allowed to be a part of the army in sections like
      <a href="/wiki/Intelligence" title="Intelligence">
       intelligence
      </a>
      , headquarters,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Signals_(military)" title="Signals (military)">
       signals
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_operations" title="Military operations">
       operations
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        [90]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Subdivisions">
       Subdivisions
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_provinces_of_Nepal" title="List of provinces of Nepal">
       List of provinces of Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Provinces_of_Nepal_2015.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3270" data-file-width="4902" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Provinces_of_Nepal_2015.png/350px-Provinces_of_Nepal_2015.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Provinces_of_Nepal_2015.png/525px-Provinces_of_Nepal_2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Provinces_of_Nepal_2015.png/700px-Provinces_of_Nepal_2015.png 2x" width="350"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">

        The administrative subdivisions of Nepal (provinces and districts).

      <a href="/wiki/List_of_districts_of_Nepal" title="List of districts of Nepal">
       75 districts
      </a>
      .
