     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
       Economy
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Nepal" title="Economy of Nepal">
       Economy of Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nepal_treemap.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="865" data-file-width="1104" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Nepal_treemap.png/350px-Nepal_treemap.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Nepal_treemap.png/525px-Nepal_treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Nepal_treemap.png/700px-Nepal_treemap.png 2x" width="350"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nepal_treemap.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A proportional representation of Nepal's exports.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kathmandu_Darbar0607_KumariGhar.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Kathmandu_Darbar0607_KumariGhar.JPG/220px-Kathmandu_Darbar0607_KumariGhar.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Kathmandu_Darbar0607_KumariGhar.JPG/330px-Kathmandu_Darbar0607_KumariGhar.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Kathmandu_Darbar0607_KumariGhar.JPG/440px-Kathmandu_Darbar0607_KumariGhar.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kathmandu_Darbar0607_KumariGhar.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Visitors at the Kathmandu Durbar
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Terraces,_south_of_Ghara_(4525876548).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1067" data-file-width="1600" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Terraces%2C_south_of_Ghara_%284525876548%29.jpg/220px-Terraces%2C_south_of_Ghara_%284525876548%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Terraces%2C_south_of_Ghara_%284525876548%29.jpg/330px-Terraces%2C_south_of_Ghara_%284525876548%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Terraces%2C_south_of_Ghara_%284525876548%29.jpg/440px-Terraces%2C_south_of_Ghara_%284525876548%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Terraces,_south_of_Ghara_(4525876548).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Terraced rice farming in Nepal
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2009-03_Kathmandu_10.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1636" data-file-width="3021" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/2009-03_Kathmandu_10.jpg/220px-2009-03_Kathmandu_10.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/2009-03_Kathmandu_10.jpg/330px-2009-03_Kathmandu_10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/2009-03_Kathmandu_10.jpg/440px-2009-03_Kathmandu_10.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2009-03_Kathmandu_10.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Tribhuvan_International_Airport" title="Tribhuvan International Airport">
         Tribhuvan International Airport
        </a>
        .
        <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Nepal" title="Tourism in Nepal">
         Tourism
        </a>
        is a key part of the national economy, with Nepal receiving approx. 800,000 foreign visitors each year.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
         <a href="#cite_note-91">
          [91]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Nepal's gross domestic product (GDP) for 2012 was estimated at over $17.921 billion (adjusted to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" title="Nominal GDP">
       nominal GDP
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imf2_6-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-imf2-6">
        [6]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2010, agriculture accounted for 36.1%, services comprised 48.5%, and industry 15.4% of Nepal's GDP.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Bank:_Nepal_at_a_glance.2C_2012_92-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Bank:_Nepal_at_a_glance.2C_2012-92">
        [92]
       </a>
      </sup>
      While agriculture and industry are contracting, the contribution by the service sector is increasing.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Bank:_Nepal_at_a_glance.2C_2012_92-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Bank:_Nepal_at_a_glance.2C_2012-92">
        [92]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nepal_Status_Paper_93-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Nepal_Status_Paper-93">
        [93]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Agriculture employs 76% of the workforce, services 18% and manufacturing and craft-based industry 6%. Agricultural produce – mostly grown in the Terai region bordering India – includes tea, rice, corn, wheat, sugarcane,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Root_crop" title="Root crop">
       root crops
      </a>
      , milk, and
      <a href="/wiki/Water_buffalo" title="Water buffalo">
       water buffalo
      </a>
      meat. Industry mainly involves the processing of agricultural produce, including
      <a href="/wiki/Jute" title="Jute">
       jute
      </a>
      , sugarcane, tobacco, and grain. Its workforce of about 10 million suffers from a severe shortage of skilled labor.
     </p>
     <p>
      Nepal's economic growth continues to be adversely affected by the political uncertainty. Nevertheless, real GDP growth was estimated to increase to almost 5 percent for 2011–2012. This is an improvement from the 3.5 percent GDP growth in 2010–2011 and would be the second-highest growth rate in the post-conflict era.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Bank:_Nepal-_Country_Overview_2012_94-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Bank:_Nepal-_Country_Overview_2012-94">
        [94]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Sources of growth include agriculture, construction, financial and other services. The contribution of growth by consumption fueled by remittances has declined since 2010/2011. While remittance growth slowed to 11 percent (in Nepali Rupee terms) in 2010/2011, it has since increased to 37 percent. Remittances are estimated to be equivalent to 25–30 percent of GDP. Inflation has been reduced to a three-year low of 7 percent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Bank:_Nepal-_Country_Overview_2012_94-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Bank:_Nepal-_Country_Overview_2012-94">
        [94]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The proportion of poor people has declined substantially since 2003. The percentage of people living below the international poverty line (people earning less than US$1.25 per day) has halved in seven years.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Bank:_Nepal-_Country_Overview_2012_94-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Bank:_Nepal-_Country_Overview_2012-94">
        [94]
       </a>
      </sup>
      At this measure of poverty the percentage of poor people declined from 53.1% in 2003/2004 to 24.8% in 2010/2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Bank:_Nepal-_Country_Overview_2012_94-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Bank:_Nepal-_Country_Overview_2012-94">
        [94]
       </a>
      </sup>
      With a higher poverty line of US$2 per-capita per day, poverty declined by one-quarter to 57.3%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Bank:_Nepal-_Country_Overview_2012_94-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Bank:_Nepal-_Country_Overview_2012-94">
        [94]
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the income distribution remains grossly uneven.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        [95]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In a recent survey, Nepal has performed extremely well in reducing poverty along with Rwanda and Bangladesh as the percentage of poor dropped to 44.2 percent of the population in 2011 from 64.7 percent in 2006—4.1 percentage points per year, which means that Nepal has made improvement in sectors like nutrition, child mortality, electricity, improved flooring and assets. If the progress of reducing poverty continues at this rate, then it is predicted that Nepal will halve the current poverty rate and eradicate it within the next 20 years.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        [96]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        [97]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        [98]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The spectacular landscape and diverse, exotic cultures of Nepal represent considerable potential for
      <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Nepal" title="Tourism in Nepal">
       tourism
      </a>
      , but growth in the industry has been stifled by political instability and poor infrastructure. Despite these problems, in 2012 the number of international tourists visiting Nepal was 598,204, a 10% increase on the previous year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        [99]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The tourism sector contributed nearly 3% of national GDP in 2012 and is the second-biggest foreign income earner after remittances.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        [100]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The rate of unemployment and underemployment approaches half of the working-age population. Thus many Nepali citizens move to other countries in search of work. Destinations include India, Qatar, the United States, Thailand, the United Kingdom, Saudi Arabia, Japan, Brunei Darussalam, Australia, and Canada.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Bank:Migration_and_Remittance_Factbook.2C_Nepal_101-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Bank:Migration_and_Remittance_Factbook.2C_Nepal-101">
        [101]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Bank:Migration_and_Remittance_Factbook.2C_pp.31-32_102-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Bank:Migration_and_Remittance_Factbook.2C_pp.31-32-102">
        [102]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nepal receives $50 million a year through the
      <a href="/wiki/Gurkha" title="Gurkha">
       Gurkha
      </a>
      soldiers who serve in the
      <a href="/wiki/Indian_Army" title="Indian Army">
       Indian
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">
       British
      </a>
      armies and are highly esteemed for their skill and bravery. As of 2010
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nepal&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , the total remittance value is around $3.5 billion.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Bank:Migration_and_Remittance_Factbook.2C_pp.31-32_102-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Bank:Migration_and_Remittance_Factbook.2C_pp.31-32-102">
        [102]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2009 alone, the remittance contributed to 22.9% of the nation's GDP.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Bank:Migration_and_Remittance_Factbook.2C_pp.31-32_102-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Bank:Migration_and_Remittance_Factbook.2C_pp.31-32-102">
        [102]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A long-standing economic agreement underpins a close relationship with India. The country receives foreign aid from the UK,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        [103]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        [104]
       </a>
      </sup>
      India, Japan, the US, the EU, China, Switzerland, and Scandinavian countries. Poverty is acute; per-capita income is around $1,000.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        [105]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Distribution_of_wealth" title="Distribution of wealth">
       distribution of wealth
      </a>
      among the Nepali is consistent with that in many developed and developing countries: the highest 10% of households control 39.1% of the national wealth and the lowest 10% control only 2.6%.
     </p>
     <p>
      The government's budget is about $1.153 billion, with an expenditure of $1.789 billion (FY 20005/06). The
      <a href="/wiki/Nepalese_rupee" title="Nepalese rupee">
       Nepali rupee
      </a>
      has been tied to the
      <a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee">
       Indian rupee
      </a>
      at an exchange rate of 1.6 for many years. Since the loosening of exchange rate controls in the early 1990s, the black market for foreign exchange has all but disappeared. The inflation rate has dropped to 2.9% after a period of higher inflation during the 1990s.
     </p>
     <p>
      Nepal's exports of mainly carpets, clothing,
      <a href="/wiki/Hemp" title="Hemp">
       hemp
      </a>
      , leather goods,
      <a href="/wiki/Jute" title="Jute">
       jute
      </a>
      goods and grain total $822 million. Import commodities of mainly gold, machinery and equipment, petroleum products and fertilizer total US$2 billion.
      <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
       European Union
      </a>
      (EU) (46.13%), the US (17.4%), and Germany (7.1%) are its main export partners. The European Union has emerged the largest buyer of Nepali ready-made garments (RMG). Exports to the EU accounted for "46.13 percent of the country's total garment exports".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        [106]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nepal's import partners include India (47.5%), the United Arab Emirates (11.2%), China (10.7%), Saudi Arabia (4.9%), and Singapore (4%).
     </p>
     <p>
      Besides having landlocked, rugged geography, few tangible natural resources and poor infrastructure, the ineffective post-1950 government and the long-running civil war are also factors in stunting the nation's economic growth and development.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_107-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Encarta-107">
        [107]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Development_Failure_108-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Development_Failure-108">
        [108]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Development-Conflict_Nexus_109-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Development-Conflict_Nexus-109">
        [109]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">
       Infrastructure
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">
       Energy
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Nepal" title="Energy in Nepal">
       Energy in Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kaligandaki_A_HPS_Tailrace_Channel.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="2432" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Kaligandaki_A_HPS_Tailrace_Channel.jpg/220px-Kaligandaki_A_HPS_Tailrace_Channel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Kaligandaki_A_HPS_Tailrace_Channel.jpg/330px-Kaligandaki_A_HPS_Tailrace_Channel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Kaligandaki_A_HPS_Tailrace_Channel.jpg/440px-Kaligandaki_A_HPS_Tailrace_Channel.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kaligandaki_A_HPS_Tailrace_Channel.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Middle Marshyandi Hydroelectricity Dam. Nepal has significant potential to generate
        <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">
         hydropower
        </a>
        , which it plans to export across South Asia
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The bulk of the energy in Nepal comes from fuel wood (68%), agricultural waste (15%), animal dung (8%), and imported fossil fuels (8%).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Independent_Power_Producers.27_Association.2C_Nepal_110-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Independent_Power_Producers.27_Association.2C_Nepal-110">
        [110]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAID_SARI_111-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-USAID_SARI-111">
        [111]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Except for some lignite deposits, Nepal has no known oil, gas or coal deposits. All commercial fossil fuels (mainly oil and coal) are either imported from India or from international markets routed through India and China. Fuel imports absorb over one-fourth of Nepal's foreign exchange earnings.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAID_SARI_111-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-USAID_SARI-111">
        [111]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Only about 1% energy need is fulfilled by electricity. The perennial nature of Nepali rivers and the steep gradient of the country's topography provide ideal conditions for the development of some of the world's largest hydroelectric projects. Current estimates put Nepal's economically feasible hydropower potential to be approximately 83,000 MW from 66 hydropower project sites.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAID_SARI_111-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-USAID_SARI-111">
        [111]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        [112]
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, currently Nepal has been able to exploit only about 600 MW from 20 medium to large hydropower plants and a number of small and micro hydropower plants.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Independent_Power_Producers.27_Association.2C_Nepal_110-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Independent_Power_Producers.27_Association.2C_Nepal-110">
        [110]
       </a>
      </sup>
      There are 9 major hydropower plants under construction, and additional 27 sites considered for potential development.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Independent_Power_Producers.27_Association.2C_Nepal_110-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Independent_Power_Producers.27_Association.2C_Nepal-110">
        [110]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Only about 40% of Nepal's population has access to electricity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Independent_Power_Producers.27_Association.2C_Nepal_110-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Independent_Power_Producers.27_Association.2C_Nepal-110">
        [110]
       </a>
      </sup>
      There is a great disparity between urban and rural areas. The electrification rate in urban areas is 90%, whereas the rate for rural areas is only 5%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAID_SARI_111-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-USAID_SARI-111">
        [111]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Power cuts of up to 22 hours a day take place in peak demand periods of winter and the peak electricity demand is almost the double the capability or dependable capacity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jamil_113-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jamil-113">
        [113]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The position of the power sector remains unsatisfactory because of high tariffs, high system losses, high generation costs, high overheads, over staffing, and lower domestic demand.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAID_SARI_111-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-USAID_SARI-111">
        [111]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">
       Transport
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Nepal" title="Transport in Nepal">
       Transport in Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Nepal remains isolated from the world's major land, air and sea transport routes although, within the country, aviation is in a better state, with 47 airports, 11 of them with paved runways;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_114-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-114">
        [114]
       </a>
      </sup>
      flights are frequent and support a sizable traffic. The hilly and mountainous terrain in the northern two-thirds of the country has made the building of roads and other infrastructure difficult and expensive. In 2007 there were just over 10,142 km (6,302 mi) of paved roads, and 7,140 km (4,437 mi) of unpaved road, and one 59 km (37 mi) railway line in the south.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_114-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-114">
        [114]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      There is a single reliable road route from India to the
      <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu_Valley" title="Kathmandu Valley">
       Kathmandu Valley
      </a>
      . More than one-third of its people live at least a two hours walk from the nearest all-season road; 15 out of 75 district headquarters are not connected by road. In addition, around 60% of road network and most rural roads are not operable during the rainy season.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        [115]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The only practical seaport of entry for goods bound for Kathmandu is
      <a href="/wiki/Kolkata" title="Kolkata">
       Kolkata
      </a>
      in West Bengal state of India. Internally, the poor state of development of the road system makes access to markets, schools, and health clinics a challenge.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_107-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Encarta-107">
        [107]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications_and_mass_media">
       Telecommunications and mass media
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      According to the Nepal Telecommunication Authority MIS May 2012 report,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NTA_MIS_Report.2C_May_2012_116-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NTA_MIS_Report.2C_May_2012-116">
        [116]
       </a>
      </sup>
      there are seven operators and the total voice telephony subscribers including fixed and mobile are 16,350,946 which gives a penetration rate of 61.42%. The fixed telephone service account for 9.37%, mobile for 64.63%, and other services (LM, GMPCS) for 3.76% of the total penetration rate. Similarly, the numbers of subscribers to data/internet services are 4,667,536 which represents 17.53% penetration rate. Most of the data service is accounted by GPRS users. Twelve months earlier the data/internet penetration was 10.05%, thus this represents a growth rate of 74.77%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NTA_MIS_Report.2C_May_2012_116-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NTA_MIS_Report.2C_May_2012-116">
        [116]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Not only has there been strong subscriber growth, especially in the mobile sector, but there was evidence of a clear vision in the sector, including putting a reform process in place and planning for the building of necessary telecommunications infrastructure. Most importantly, the Ministry of Information and Communications (MoIC) and the telecom regulator, the National Telecommunications Authority (NTA), have both been very active in the performance of their respective roles.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nepal_ICT_Forecasts_117-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Nepal_ICT_Forecasts-117">
        [117]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Despite all the effort, there remained a significant disparity between the high coverage levels in the cities and the coverage available in the underdeveloped rural regions. Progress on providing some minimum access had been good. Of a total of 3,914 village development committees across the country, 306 were unserved by December 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nepal_ICT_Forecasts_117-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Nepal_ICT_Forecasts-117">
        [117]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In order to meet future demand, it was estimated that Nepal needed to invest around US$135 million annually in its telecom sector.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nepal_ICT_Forecasts_117-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Nepal_ICT_Forecasts-117">
        [117]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2009, the telecommunication sector alone contributed to 1% of the nation's GDP.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Bank.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Nepal.27s_ICT_at_a_glance_118-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Bank.C2.A0.E2.80.94_Nepal.27s_ICT_at_a_glance-118">
        [118]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of 30 September 2012, Nepal has 1,828,700 Facebook users.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Internet_Stats_119-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Internet_Stats-119">
        [119]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of 2007
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nepal&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , the state operates two television stations as well as national and regional radio stations. There are roughly 30 independent TV channels registered, with only about half in regular operation. Nearly 400 FM radio stations are licensed with roughly 300 operational.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_114-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-114">
        [114]
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to the 2011 census, the percentage of households possessing radio was 50.82%, television 36.45%, cable TV 19.33%, computer 7.23%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pre-cen_5-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-pre-cen-5">
        [5]
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to the Press Council Nepal, as of 2012
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nepal&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      there are 2,038 registered newspapers in Nepal, among which 514 are in publication.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Press_Council_Nepal_120-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Press_Council_Nepal-120">
        [120]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2013,
      <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">
       Reporters Without Borders
      </a>
      ranked Nepal at 118th place in the world in terms of press freedom.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        [121]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        [122]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
       Education
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Nepal" title="Education in Nepal">
       Education in Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The overall literacy rate (for population age 5 years and above) increased from 54.1% in 2001 to 65.9% in 2011. The male literacy rate was 75.1% compared to the female literacy rate of 57.4%. The highest literacy rate was reported in Kathmandu district (86.3%) and lowest in
      <a href="/wiki/Rautahat_District" title="Rautahat District">
       Rautahat
      </a>
      (41.7%).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pre-cen_5-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-pre-cen-5">
        [5]
       </a>
      </sup>
      While the net primary enrollment rate was 74% in 2005;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-undp_123-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-undp-123">
        [123]
       </a>
      </sup>
      in 2009, that enrollment rate was 90%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldbank_124-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-worldbank-124">
        [124]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      However, increasing access to secondary education (grade 9–12) remains a major challenge, as evidenced by the low net enrollment rate of 24% at this level. More than half of primary students do not enter secondary schools, and only one-half of them complete secondary schooling. In addition, fewer girls than boys join secondary schools and, among those who do, fewer complete the 10th grade.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
       <a href="#cite_note-125">
        [125]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Nepal has seven universities:
      <a href="/wiki/Tribhuvan_University" title="Tribhuvan University">
       Tribhuvan University
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu_University" title="Kathmandu University">
       Kathmandu University
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Pokhara_University" title="Pokhara University">
       Pokhara University
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Purbanchal_University" title="Purbanchal University">
       Purbanchal University
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahendra_Sanskrit_University" title="Mahendra Sanskrit University">
       Mahendra Sanskrit University
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Far-western_University" title="Far-western University">
       Far-western University
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_and_Forestry_University" title="Agriculture and Forestry University">
       Agriculture and Forestry University
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
       <a href="#cite_note-126">
        [126]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Some newly proposed universities are Lumbini Bouddha University, and Mid-Western University. Some fine scholarship has emerged in the post-1990 era.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        [127]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Health">
       Health
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Nepal" title="Health in Nepal">
       Health in Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kunde_Hospital_IMG_1688a.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Kunde_Hospital_IMG_1688a.jpg/220px-Kunde_Hospital_IMG_1688a.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Kunde_Hospital_IMG_1688a.jpg/330px-Kunde_Hospital_IMG_1688a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Kunde_Hospital_IMG_1688a.jpg/440px-Kunde_Hospital_IMG_1688a.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kunde_Hospital_IMG_1688a.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Kunde Hospital in remote Himalayan region
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Public health and health care services in Nepal are provided by both the public and private sectors and fare poorly by international standards.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      According to 2011 census, more than one-third (38.17%) of the total households do not have a toilet.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pre-cen_5-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-pre-cen-5">
        [5]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Tap water is the main source of drinking water for 47.78% of households, tube well/hand pump is the main source of drinking water for about 35% of households, while spout, uncovered well/
      <i>
       kuwa
      </i>
      , and covered well/
      <i>
       kuwa
      </i>
      are the main source for 5.74%, 4.71%, and 2.45% respectively.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pre-cen_5-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-pre-cen-5">
        [5]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Based on 2010 World Health Organization (WHO) data, Nepal ranked 139th in life expectancy in 2010 with the average Nepali living to 65.8 years.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        [128]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO_Nepal_Fact_Sheet_129-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WHO_Nepal_Fact_Sheet-129">
        [129]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Diseases are more prevalent in Nepal than in other South Asian countries, especially in rural areas. Leading diseases and illnesses include
      <a href="/wiki/Diarrhea" title="Diarrhea">
       diarrhea
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gastrointestinal_disorders" title="Gastrointestinal disorders">
       gastrointestinal disorders
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Goitre" title="Goitre">
       goitres
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intestinal_parasites" title="Intestinal parasites">
       intestinal parasites
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Leprosy" title="Leprosy">
       leprosy
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Visceral_leishmaniasis" title="Visceral leishmaniasis">
       visceral leishmaniasis
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">
       tuberculosis
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MoHP_Factsheet_130-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-MoHP_Factsheet-130">
        [130]
       </a>
      </sup>
      About 4 out of 1,000 adults aged 15 to 49 had
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_immunodeficiency_virus" title="Human immunodeficiency virus">
       human immunodeficiency virus
      </a>
      (HIV), and the HIV prevalence rate was 0.5%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO_Nepal_Health_Profile_131-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WHO_Nepal_Health_Profile-131">
        [131]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO_Epidemiological_Fact_Sheet_on_HIV_and_AIDS_132-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WHO_Epidemiological_Fact_Sheet_on_HIV_and_AIDS-132">
        [132]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">
       Malnutrition
      </a>
      also remains very high: about 47% of children under five are stunted, 15 percent wasted, and 36 percent underweight, although there has been a declining trend for these rates over the past five years, they remain alarmingly high.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
       <a href="#cite_note-133">
        [133]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In spite of these figures, improvements in health care have been made, most notably in maternal-child health. In 2012, the under-five infant mortality was estimated to be 41 out of every 1000 children.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO_Trend_in_Health_Status_134-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WHO_Trend_in_Health_Status-134">
        [134]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Bank_Health_Services_in_Nepal_135-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Bank_Health_Services_in_Nepal-135">
        [135]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Overall Nepal's Human Development Index (HDI) for health was 0.77 in 2011, ranking Nepal 126 out of 194 countries, up from 0.444 in 1980.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HDI_Trend_136-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HDI_Trend-136">
        [136]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
       <a href="#cite_note-137">
        [137]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Community_forestry">
       Community forestry
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The Community Forestry Program in Nepal is a participatory environmental governance that encompasses well-defined policies, institutions, and practices. The program addresses the twin goals of forest conservation and poverty reduction. As more than 70 percent of Nepal's population depends on agriculture for their livelihood, community management of forests has been a critically important intervention. Through legislative developments and operational innovations over three decades, the program has evolved from a protection-oriented, conservation-focused agenda to a much more broad-based strategy for forest use, enterprise development, and livelihood improvement. By April 2009, one-third of Nepal's population was participating in the program, directly managing more than one-fourth of Nepal's forest area.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Community_forestry_in_Nepal.2C_IFPRI_138-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Community_forestry_in_Nepal.2C_IFPRI-138">
        [138]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forestry_Nepal_139-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Forestry_Nepal-139">
        [139]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The immediate livelihood benefits derived by rural households bolster strong collective action wherein local communities actively and sustainably manage forest resources. Community forests also became the source of diversified investment capital and raw material for new market-oriented livelihoods. Community forestry shows traits of political, financial, and ecological sustainability, including an emergence of a strong legal and regulatory framework, and robust civil society institutions and networks. However, a continuing challenge is to ensure equitable distribution of benefits to women and marginalized groups. Lessons for replication emphasize experiential learning, establishment of a strong civil society network, flexible regulation to encourage diverse institutional modalities, and responsiveness of government and policymakers to a multistakeholder collaborative learning process.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Community_Forestry_in_Nepal.2C_Satoyama_140-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Community_Forestry_in_Nepal.2C_Satoyama-140">
        [140]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forestry_Nepal.2C_IRIN_141-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Forestry_Nepal.2C_IRIN-141">
        [141]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">
       Science and technology
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Nepal" title="Science and technology in Nepal">
       Science and technology in Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nyatapola_Temple.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Nyatapola_Temple.JPG/220px-Nyatapola_Temple.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Nyatapola_Temple.JPG/330px-Nyatapola_Temple.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Nyatapola_Temple.JPG/440px-Nyatapola_Temple.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nyatapola_Temple.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Erected by King Bhupatindra Malla in 1702,
        <a href="/wiki/Nyatapola" title="Nyatapola">
         Nyatapola
        </a>
        is an important tourist attraction in the historical city of
        <a href="/wiki/Bhaktapur" title="Bhaktapur">
         Bhaktapur
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Historical kingdoms that existed in the Kathmandu valley are found to have made use of some clever technologies in numerous areas such as architecture, agriculture, civil engineering, water management, etc. The Gopals and Abhirs, who ruled the valley up until
      <abbr title="circa">
       c.
      </abbr>
      1000 BC, used temporary materials for construction such as bamboo, hay, timber, etc. The
      <a href="/wiki/Kirata_Kingdom" title="Kirata Kingdom">
       Kirat
      </a>
      period (700 BC – 110 AD) employed the technology of brick firing as well as produced quality woolen shawls. Similarly,
      <a href="/wiki/Stupa" title="Stupa">
       stupas
      </a>
      , idols, canals, self-recharging ponds, reservoirs, etc. constructed during the
      <a href="/wiki/Licchavi_(kingdom)" title="Licchavi (kingdom)">
       Lichhavi
      </a>
      era (110 AD – 879 AD) are intact to this day, which manifests the ingenuity of traditional architecture. Moreover, the
      <a href="/wiki/Malla_(Nepal)" title="Malla (Nepal)">
       Malla
      </a>
      period (1200 AD – 1768 AD) saw an impressive growth in architecture, on par with its advanced contemporaries. An archetypal example of Malla architecture is
      <a href="/wiki/Nyatapola" title="Nyatapola">
       Nyatapola
      </a>
      , a five-storied, 30-meter tall temple in Bhaktapur that has strangely survived at least four major earthquakes, including the
      <a href="/wiki/April_2015_Nepal_earthquake" title="April 2015 Nepal earthquake">
       April 2015 Nepal earthquake
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unesco_142-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-unesco-142">
        [142]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Nepal was a late entrant into the modern world of science and technology. Nepal’s first institution of higher education,
      <a href="/wiki/Tri-Chandra_College" title="Tri-Chandra College">
       Tri-Chandra College
      </a>
      , was established by
      <a href="/wiki/Chandra_Shumsher_Jang_Bahadur_Rana" title="Chandra Shumsher Jang Bahadur Rana">
       Chandra Shumsher
      </a>
      in 1918. The college introduced science at the Intermediate level a year later, marking the genesis of formal
      <a href="/wiki/Science_education" title="Science education">
       science education
      </a>
      in the country.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unesco_142-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-unesco-142">
        [142]
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the college was not accessible to the general public, but only to a handful of members of the
      <a href="/wiki/Rana_dynasty" title="Rana dynasty">
       Rana regime
      </a>
      . Throughout the Rana regime that lasted for well over a century, Nepal was effectively isolated from the rest of the world. Owing to this isolation, Nepal was relatively untouched by and unfamiliar of social transformations brought about by the
      <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">
       British invasion
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">
       India
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">
       Industrial Revolution
      </a>
      in the West.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts_143-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-sts-143">
        [143]
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, after the advent of democracy and abolition of Rana regime in 1951, Nepal broke free from the shackles of self-imposed isolation and opened up to the outside world. This opening marked the initiation of S&amp;T activities in the country.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unesco1_144-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-unesco1-144">
        [144]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      An underdeveloped country, Nepal is plagued with problems like
      <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">
       poverty
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illiteracy" title="Illiteracy">
       illiteracy
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">
       unemployment
      </a>
      , etc. Consequently, science and technology have invariably lagged behind in the priority list of the government. On the other hand, citing poor university education at home, tens of thousands of Nepali students leave the country every year, with half of them never returning.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
       <a href="#cite_note-145">
        [145]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
       <a href="#cite_note-146">
        [146]
       </a>
      </sup>
      These factors have been huge deterrents to the development of science and technology in Nepal.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Crime_and_law_enforcement">
       Crime and law enforcement
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Nepal" title="Law enforcement in Nepal">
       Law enforcement in Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Directorate_of_Military_Intelligence,_Nepal" title="Directorate of Military Intelligence, Nepal">
       Directorate of Military Intelligence, Nepal
      </a>
      ;
      <a href="/wiki/National_Investigation_Department_of_Nepal" title="National Investigation Department of Nepal">
       National Investigation Department of Nepal
      </a>
      ; and
      <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking_in_Nepal" title="Human trafficking in Nepal">
       Human trafficking in Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Law enforcement in Nepal is primarily the responsibility of the Nepali Police Force which is the national police of Nepal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPD_147-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NPD-147">
        [147]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is independent of the
      <a href="/wiki/Nepalese_Army" title="Nepalese Army">
       Nepali Army
      </a>
      . In the days of its establishment, Nepal Police personnel were mainly drawn from the armed forces of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nepali_Congress_Party" title="Nepali Congress Party">
       Nepali Congress Party
      </a>
      which fought against the feudal
      <a href="/wiki/Rana_dynasty" title="Rana dynasty">
       Rana
      </a>
      autocracy in Nepal. The
      <a href="/wiki/Central_Investigation_Bureau" title="Central Investigation Bureau">
       Central Investigation Bureau
      </a>
      (CIB) and
      <a href="/wiki/National_Investigation_Department_of_Nepal" title="National Investigation Department of Nepal">
       National Investigation Department of Nepal
      </a>
      (NID) are the investigation agencies of Nepal. They have offices in all 75 administrative districts including regional offices in five regions and zonal offices in 14 zones. Numbers vary from three to five members at each district level in rural districts, and numbers can be higher in urban districts. They have both Domestic and International surveillance unit which mainly deals with cross border terrorists, drug trafficking and money laundering.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newman2010_148-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Newman2010-148">
        [148]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AHRC_149-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-AHRC-149">
        [149]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InterpolNepal_150-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-InterpolNepal-150">
        [150]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown2013_151-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Brown2013-151">
        [151]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A 2010 survey estimated about 46,000 hard drug users in the country, with 70% of the users to be within the age group of 15 to 29.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aryal2010_152-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Aryal2010-152">
        [152]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The same survey also reported that 19% of the users had been introduced to hard drugs when they were less than 15 years old; and 14.4% of drug users were attending school or college.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aryal2010_152-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Aryal2010-152">
        [152]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Only 12 of the 17 municipalities studied had any type of rehabilitation center.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aryal2010_152-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Aryal2010-152">
        [152]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-narconon_153-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-narconon-153">
        [153]
       </a>
      </sup>
      There has been a sharp increase in the seizure of drugs such as hashish, heroin and opium in the past few years; and there are indications that drug traffickers are trying to establish Nepal as a transit point.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ethirajan2013_154-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Ethirajan2013-154">
        [154]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking_in_Nepal" title="Human trafficking in Nepal">
       Human trafficking
      </a>
      is a major problem in Nepal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams2013_155-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Williams2013-155">
        [155]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TinyHands_156-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-TinyHands-156">
        [156]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MaitiNepal_157-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-MaitiNepal-157">
        [157]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nepali victims are trafficked within Nepal, to India, the Middle East, and other areas such as Malaysia and forced to become prostitutes, domestic servants, beggars, factory workers, mine workers, circus performers, child soldiers, and others. Sex trafficking is particularly rampant within Nepal and to India, with as many as 5,000 to 10,000 women and girls trafficked to India alone each year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sangroula2001_158-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Sangroula2001-158">
        [158]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABA2011_159-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ABA2011-159">
        [159]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHRC2010_160-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NHRC2010-160">
        [160]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      With wider availability of information technology,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyber_crime" title="Cyber crime">
       cyber crime
      </a>
      is a growing trend. The police handled 16 cases of cyber crime in fiscal year 2010/2011, 47 cases in 2011/2012 and 78 in the current fiscal year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pariyar2013_161-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Pariyar2013-161">
        [161]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
         <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2015)">
          clarification needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Capital punishment was abolished in Nepal in 1997.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Death_Penalty_162-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Death_Penalty-162">
        [162]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2008, the Nepali government abolished the
      <a href="/wiki/Haliya" title="Haliya">
       Haliya
      </a>
      system of forced labour, freeing about 20,000 people.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
       <a href="#cite_note-163">
        [163]
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the effectiveness of this has been questioned by the Asian Legal Resource Centre.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
       <a href="#cite_note-164">
        [164]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
       Demographics
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Nepal" title="Demographics of Nepal">
       Demographics of Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Newar_gentlemen_of_Kathmandu_1940.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="1200" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Newar_gentlemen_of_Kathmandu_1940.jpg/220px-Newar_gentlemen_of_Kathmandu_1940.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Newar_gentlemen_of_Kathmandu_1940.jpg/330px-Newar_gentlemen_of_Kathmandu_1940.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Newar_gentlemen_of_Kathmandu_1940.jpg/440px-Newar_gentlemen_of_Kathmandu_1940.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Newar_gentlemen_of_Kathmandu_1940.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Nepalese gentlemen in 1940
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teej.jpg">

       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">

         </a>
        </div>
        Nepalese women dancing for
        <a href="/wiki/Teej" title="Teej">
         Teej
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Population_density_map_of_nepal.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="636" data-file-width="1053" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Population_density_map_of_nepal.png/220px-Population_density_map_of_nepal.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Population_density_map_of_nepal.png/330px-Population_density_map_of_nepal.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Population_density_map_of_nepal.png/440px-Population_density_map_of_nepal.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Population_density_map_of_nepal.png" title="Enlarge">

        Population density map of Nepal
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NepalPopulationEnglishGraph.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1052" data-file-width="744" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/NepalPopulationEnglishGraph.svg/220px-NepalPopulationEnglishGraph.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/NepalPopulationEnglishGraph.svg/330px-NepalPopulationEnglishGraph.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/NepalPopulationEnglishGraph.svg/440px-NepalPopulationEnglishGraph.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NepalPopulationEnglishGraph.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Comparison Of Nepal Population
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      According to the 2011 census, Nepal's population grew from 9 million people in 1950 to 26.5 million. From 2001 to 2011, the average family size declined from 5.44 to 4.9. The census also noted some 1.9 million absentee people, over a million more than in 2001; most are male laborers employed overseas, predominantly in South Asia and the Middle East. This correlated with the drop in sex ratio from 94.41 as compared to 99.80 for 2001. The annual population growth rate is 1.35%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pre-cen_5-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-pre-cen-5">
        [5]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The citizens of Nepal are known as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nepali_people" title="Nepali people">
       Nepali
      </a>
      or Nepalese. The country is home to people of many different national origins. As a result,
      <i>
       Nepalese
      </i>
      do not equate their nationality with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Nepal" title="Ethnic groups in Nepal">
       ethnicity
      </a>
      , but with
      <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">
       citizenship
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Allegiance" title="Allegiance">
       allegiance
      </a>
      . Although citizens make up the majority of Nepalese, non-citizen residents, dual citizens, and expatriates may also claim a Nepalese identity. Nepal is multicultural and multiethnic country because it became a country by occupying several small kingdoms such as
      <a href="/wiki/Mustang_District" title="Mustang District">
       Mustang
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Videha" title="Videha">
       Videha
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Mithila_(ancient)" title="Mithila (ancient)">
       Mithila
      </a>
      ),
      <a href="/wiki/Madhesh" title="Madhesh">
       Madhesh
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Limbuwan" title="Limbuwan">
       Limbuwan
      </a>
      in the 18th century. The oldest settlements in
      <a href="/wiki/Mithila,_Nepal" title="Mithila, Nepal">
       Mithila
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Tharuhat" title="Tharuhat">
       Tharuhat
      </a>
      are indigenous
      <a href="/wiki/Maithil" title="Maithil">
       Maithil
      </a>
      and aboriginal
      <a href="/wiki/Tharu_people" title="Tharu people">
       Tharu people
      </a>
      . Northern Nepal is historically inhabited by Kirants
      <a href="/wiki/Mongoloid" title="Mongoloid">
       Mongoloid
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rai_(ethnic_group)" title="Rai (ethnic group)">
       Rai
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Limbu" title="Limbu">
       Limbu
      </a>
      people. The mountainous region is sparsely populated above 3,000 m (9,800 ft), but in central and western Nepal ethnic
      <a href="/wiki/Sherpa_people" title="Sherpa people">
       Sherpa
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Lama" title="Lama">
       Lamapeople
      </a>
      inhabit even higher semi-arid valleys north of the Himalaya.
      <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu_Valley" title="Kathmandu Valley">
       Kathmandu Valley
      </a>
      , in the middle hill region, constitutes a small fraction of the nation's area but is the most densely populated, with almost 5 percent of the nation's population. The Nepali are descendants of three major migrations from India,
      <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">
       Tibet
      </a>
      , and North Burma and the Chinese province of
      <a href="/wiki/Yunnan" title="Yunnan">
       Yunnan
      </a>
      via
      <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">
       Assam
      </a>
      . Among the earliest inhabitants were the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kirat" title="Kirat">
       Kirat
      </a>
      of east mid-region,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newar" title="Newar">
       Newars
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Kathmandu_Valley" title="Kathmandu Valley">
       Kathmandu Valley
      </a>
      , aboriginal
      <a href="/wiki/Tharu_people" title="Tharu people">
       Tharus
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Tharuhat" title="Tharuhat">
       Tharuhat
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Madhesi_people" title="Madhesi people">
       Madhesis
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Madhesh" title="Madhesh">
       Madhesh
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Maithil" title="Maithil">
       Maithils
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Mithila,_Nepal" title="Mithila, Nepal">
       Mithila
      </a>
      region.
      <i>
       Ancient and Indigenous
       <a href="/wiki/Madhesi_people" title="Madhesi people">
        Madhesis
       </a>
      </i>
      are descendents of Nepalese origin tribes while
      <i>
       Indian origin
       <a href="/wiki/Madhesi_people" title="Madhesi people">
        Madhesis
       </a>
      </i>
      are the descendents of Nepalese migrants to
      <a href="/wiki/Madhesh" title="Madhesh">
       Madhesh
      </a>
      from Indian state of
      <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">
       Bihar
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uttar_pradesh" title="Uttar pradesh">
       Uttar pradesh
      </a>
      ; the
      <a href="/wiki/Brahmin" title="Brahmin">
       Brahmin
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Bahun" title="Bahun">
       Bahun
      </a>
      ) and
      <a href="/wiki/Kshatriya" title="Kshatriya">
       Kshatriya
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Chettri" title="Chettri">
       Chettri
      </a>
      ) caste groups are descendents of migrants from India's present
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Banaras" title="Banaras">
       Banaras
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kumaon_division" title="Kumaon division">
       Kumaon
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garhwal_Division" title="Garhwal Division">
       Garhwal
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Kashmir" title="Kashmir">
       Kashmir
      </a>
      regions, while other ethnic groups trace their origins to North Burma and
      <a href="/wiki/Yunnan" title="Yunnan">
       Yunnan
      </a>
      and Tibet, e.g., the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gurung" title="Gurung">
       Gurung
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magar_people" title="Magar people">
       Magar
      </a>
      in the west,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rai_(Ethnic_Group)" title="Rai (Ethnic Group)">
       Rai
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunuwar_people" title="Sunuwar people">
       Sunuwar
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Limbu_people" title="Limbu people">
       Limbu
      </a>
      in the east (from Yunnan and north Burma via Assam), and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sherpa_(people)" title="Sherpa (people)">
       Sherpa
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Bhutia" title="Bhutia">
       Bhutia
      </a>
      in the north (from Tibet).
     </p>
     <p>
      Despite the migration of a significant section of the population to the
      <a href="/wiki/Madhesh" title="Madhesh">
       Madhesh
      </a>
      (southern plains) in recent years, the majority of Nepalese still live in the central highlands; the northern mountains are sparsely populated. Kathmandu, with a population of over 2.6 million (metropolitan area: 5 million),
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Disputed statement">
         <span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (April 2015)">
          dubious
         </span>
        </a>
        <span class="metadata">
         –
         <a href="/wiki/Talk:Nepal#Dubious" title="Talk:Nepal">
          discuss
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      is the largest city in the country and the cultural and economic heart.
     </p>
     <p>
      According to the
      <i>
       World Refugee Survey 2008
      </i>
      , published by the US Committee for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Refugees" title="Refugees">
       Refugees
      </a>
      and Immigrants, Nepal hosted a population of refugees and asylum seekers in 2007 numbering approximately 130,000. Of this population, approximately 109,200 persons were from Bhutan and 20,500 from People's Republic of China.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_165-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-165">
        [165]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
       <a href="#cite_note-166">
        [166]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The government of Nepal restricted
      <a href="/wiki/Bhutanese_refugees" title="Bhutanese refugees">
       Bhutanese refugees
      </a>
      to seven camps in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jhapa" title="Jhapa">
       Jhapa
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morang" title="Morang">
       Morang
      </a>
      districts, and refugees were not permitted to work in most professions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_165-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-165">
        [165]
       </a>
      </sup>
      At present, the United States is working towards resettling more than 60,000 of these refugees in the US.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bhutan_44-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bhutan-44">
        [44]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
       Languages
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Nepal" title="Languages of Nepal">
       Languages of Nepal
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Nepal's diverse linguistic heritage stems from three major language groups:
      <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">
       Indo-Aryan
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tibeto-Burman" title="Tibeto-Burman">
       Tibeto-Burman
      </a>
      , and various
      <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_language" title="Indigenous language">
       indigenous language
      </a>
      isolates. The major languages of Nepal (percent spoken as native language) according to the 2011 census are
      <a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">
       Nepali
      </a>
      (44.6%),
      <a href="/wiki/Maithili_language" title="Maithili language">
       Maithili
      </a>
      (11.7%),
      <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri_language" title="Bhojpuri language">
       Bhojpuri (Awadhi Language)
      </a>
      (6.0%),
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tharu_language" title="Tharu language">
       Tharu
      </a>
      (5.8%),
      <a href="/wiki/Tamang_language" title="Tamang language">
       Tamang
      </a>
      (5.1%),
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nepal_Bhasa" title="Nepal Bhasa">
       Nepal Bhasa
      </a>
      (3.2%),
      <a href="/wiki/Bajjika_dialect" title="Bajjika dialect">
       Bajjika
      </a>
      (3%) and
      <a href="/wiki/Magar_language" title="Magar language">
       Magar
      </a>
      (3.0%),
      <a href="/wiki/Doteli_language" title="Doteli language">
       Doteli
      </a>
      (3.0%),
      <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">
       Urdu
      </a>
      (2.6%) and
      <a href="/wiki/Sunwar_language" title="Sunwar language">
       Sunwar
      </a>
      . Nepal is home to at least four indigenous
      <a href="/wiki/Nepali_Sign_Language" title="Nepali Sign Language">
       sign languages
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Derived from
      <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">
       Sanskrit
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">
       Nepali
      </a>
      is written in
      <a href="/wiki/Devanagari" title="Devanagari">
       Devanagari
      </a>
      script. Nepali is the official language and serves as
      <i>
       lingua franca
      </i>
      among Nepali of different ethnolinguistic groups. The regional languages
      <a href="/wiki/Maithili_language" title="Maithili language">
       Maithili
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Awadhi_language" title="Awadhi language">
       Awadhi
      </a>
      , Bhojpuri and rarely
      <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">
       Urdu
      </a>
      of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nepali_Muslims" title="Nepali Muslims">
       Nepali Muslims
      </a>
      are spoken in the southern
      <a href="/wiki/Madhesh" title="Madhesh">
       Madhesh
      </a>
      region. Many Nepali in government and business speak
      <a href="/wiki/Maithili_language" title="Maithili language">
       Maithili
      </a>
      as the main language and
      <a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">
       Nepali
      </a>
      as their de facto
      <i>
       lingua franca
      </i>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Tibetic_languages" title="Tibetic languages">
       Varieties of Tibetan
      </a>
      are spoken in and north of the higher Himalaya where standard literary Tibetan is widely understood by those with religious education. Local dialects in the Terai and hills are mostly unwritten with efforts underway to develop systems for writing many in Devanagari or the Roman alphabet.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
       Religion
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">

         <a href="/wiki/Kirant_Mundhum" title="Kirant Mundhum">
          Folk
         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
         <div style="background:red; width:3.0%; overflow: hidden;">
         </div>
        </td>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
         3.0%
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
         <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Nepal" title="Christianity in Nepal">
          Christian
         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
         <div style="background:blue; width:1.42%; overflow: hidden;">
         </div>
        </td>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
         1.42%
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
         <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion_in_Nepal" title="Freedom of religion in Nepal">
          Other
         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
         <div style="background:gray; width:0.9%; overflow: hidden;">
         </div>
        </td>
        <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
         0.9%
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
     </div>
     <p>
      The overwhelming majority of the Nepalese population follows
      <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">
       Hinduism
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Shiva" title="Shiva">
       Shiva
      </a>
      is regarded as the guardian deity of the country.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
       <a href="#cite_note-168">
        [168]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nepal is home to the famous Lord Shiva temple, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pashupatinath_temple" title="Pashupatinath temple">
       Pashupatinath
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Hindu_temple" title="Hindu temple">
       Temple
      </a>
      , where Hindus from all over the world come for pilgrimage. According to Hindu mythology, the goddess
      <a href="/wiki/Sita" title="Sita">
       Sita
      </a>
      of the epic
      <a href="/wiki/Ramayana" title="Ramayana">
       Ramayana
      </a>
      , was born in the Mithila Kingdom of King Janaka Raja.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Lumbini" title="Lumbini">
       Lumbini
      </a>
      is a
      <a href="/wiki/Buddhist_pilgrimage" title="Buddhist pilgrimage">
       Buddhist pilgrimage
      </a>
      site and UNESCO
      <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
       World Heritage Site
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Kapilavastu" title="Kapilavastu">
       Kapilavastu
      </a>
      district. Traditionally it is held to be the birthplace in about 563 B.C. of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siddhartha_Gautama" title="Siddhartha Gautama">
       Siddhartha Gautama
      </a>
      , a Kshatriya caste prince of the Sakya clan, who as the
      <a href="/wiki/Gautama_Buddha" title="Gautama Buddha">
       Buddha Gautama
      </a>
      , founded
      <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
       Buddhism
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The holy site of Lumbini is bordered by a large monastic zone, in which only monasteries can be built. All three main branches of Buddhism exist in Nepal and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newa_people" title="Newa people">
       Newa people
      </a>
      have their own
      <a href="/wiki/Newar_Buddhism" title="Newar Buddhism">
       branch
      </a>
      of the faith.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
       <a href="#cite_note-169">
        [169]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Buddhism is also the dominant religion of the thinly populated northern areas, which are mostly inhabited by Tibetan-related peoples, such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Sherpa_people" title="Sherpa people">
       Sherpa
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The Buddha, born as a
      <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">
       Hindu
      </a>
      , is also said to be a descendant of
      <a href="/wiki/Vedas" title="Vedas">
       Vedic
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Angiras_(sage)" title="Angiras (sage)">
       Sage Angirasa
      </a>
      in many Buddhist texts.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
       <a href="#cite_note-170">
        [170]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Buddha's family surname is associated with
      <a href="/wiki/Gautama_Maharishi" title="Gautama Maharishi">
       Gautama Maharishi
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">
       <a href="#cite_note-171">
        [171]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Differences between Hindus and Buddhists have been minimal in Nepal due to the cultural and historical intermingling of Hindu and Buddhist beliefs. Moreover, traditionally Buddhism and Hinduism were never two distinct religions in the western sense of the word. In Nepal, the faiths share common temples and worship common deities. Among other natives of Nepal, those more influenced by Hinduism were the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magar_people" title="Magar people">
       Magar
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunwar" title="Sunwar">
       Sunwar
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Limbu_people" title="Limbu people">
       Limbu
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rai_(ethnic_group)" title="Rai (ethnic group)">
       Rai
      </a>
      and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gurkhas" title="Gurkhas">
       Gurkhas
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Library_of_Congress_33-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Library_of_Congress-33">
        [33]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Hindu influence is less prominent among the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gurung" title="Gurung">
       Gurung
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Bhutia" title="Bhutia">
       Bhutia
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Thakali_people" title="Thakali people">
       Thakali
      </a>
      groups who employ Buddhist monks for their religious ceremonies.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Library_of_Congress_33-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Library_of_Congress-33">
        [33]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Most of the festivals in Nepal are Hindu.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Festivals_of_Nepal_172-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Festivals_of_Nepal-172">
        [172]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Machendrajatra festival, dedicated to Hindu
      <a href="/wiki/Shaivism" title="Shaivism">
       Shaiva
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Siddha" title="Siddha">
       Siddha
      </a>
      , is celebrated by many Buddhists in Nepal as a main festival.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">
       <a href="#cite_note-173">
        [173]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As it is believed that Ne Muni established Nepal,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">
       <a href="#cite_note-174">
        [174]
       </a>
      </sup>
      some important priests in Nepal are called "Tirthaguru Nemuni".
      <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Nepal" title="Islam in Nepal">
       Islam
      </a>
      is a minority religion in Nepal, with 4.2% of the population being Muslim according to a 2006
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People_of_Nepal" title="People of Nepal">
       Nepali
      </a>
      census.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">
       <a href="#cite_note-175">
        [175]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Kirant_Mundhum" title="Kirant Mundhum">
       Mundhum
      </a>
      , Christianity and
      <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">
       Jainism
      </a>
      are other minority faiths.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176">
       <a href="#cite_note-176">
        [176]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
